    46	
    47	## What Is This
    48	
    49	Career-Ops turns any AI coding CLI into a full job search command center. Instead of manually tracking applications in a spreadsheet, you get an AI-powered pipeline that:
    50	
    51	- **Evaluates offers** with a structured A-F scoring system (10 weighted dimensions)
    52	- **Generates tailored PDFs** -- ATS-optimized CVs customized per job description
    53	- **Scans portals** automatically (Greenhouse, Ashby, Lever, company pages)
    54	- **Processes in batch** -- evaluate 10+ offers in parallel with sub-agents
    55	- **Tracks everything** in a single source of truth with integrity checks
    56	
    57	> **Important: This is NOT a spray-and-pray tool.** Career-ops is a filter -- it helps you find the few offers worth your time out of hundreds. The system strongly recommends against applying to anything scoring below 4.0/5. Your time is valuable, and so is the recruiter's. Always review before submitting.
    58	
    59	Career-ops is agentic: Claude Code navigates career pages with Playwright, evaluates fit by reasoning about your CV vs the job description (not keyword matching), and adapts your resume per listing.
    60	
    61	> **Heads up: the first evaluations won't be great.** The system doesn't know you yet. Feed it context -- your CV, your career story, your proof points, your preferences, what you're good at, what you want to avoid. The more you nurture it, the better it gets. Think of it as onboarding a new recruiter: the first week they need to learn about you, then they become invaluable.
    62	
    63	Built by someone who used it to evaluate 740+ job offers, generate 100+ tailored CVs, and land a Head of Applied AI role. [Read the full case study](https://santifer.io/career-ops-system).
    64	
    65	## Features
    66	
    67	| Feature | Description |
    68	|---------|-------------|
    69	| **Auto-Pipeline** | Paste a URL, get a full evaluation + PDF + tracker entry |
    70	| **6-Block Evaluation** | Role summary, CV match, level strategy, comp research, personalization, interview prep (STAR+R) |
    71	| **Interview Story Bank** | Accumulates STAR+Reflection stories across evaluations -- 5-10 master stories that answer any behavioral question |
    72	| **Negotiation Scripts** | Salary negotiation frameworks, geographic discount pushback, competing offer leverage |
    73	| **ATS PDF Generation** | Keyword-injected CVs with Space Grotesk + DM Sans design |
    74	| **Portal Scanner** | 45+ companies pre-configured (Anthropic, OpenAI, ElevenLabs, Retool, n8n...) + custom queries across Ashby, Greenhouse, Lever, Wellfound |
    75	| **Batch Processing** | Parallel evaluation with `claude -p` workers |
    76	| **Dashboard TUI** | Terminal UI to browse, filter, and sort your pipeline |
    77	| **Human-in-the-Loop** | AI evaluates and recommends, you decide and act. The system never submits an application -- you always have the final call |
    78	| **Pipeline Integrity** | Automated merge, dedup, status normalization, health checks |
    79	
    80	## Quick Start
    81	
    82	```bash
    83	# 1. Clone and install
    84	git clone https://github.com/santifer/career-ops.git
    85	cd career-ops && npm install
    86	npx playwright install chromium   # Required for PDF generation
    87	
    88	# 2. Check setup
    89	npm run doctor                     # Validates all prerequisites
    90	
    91	# 3. Configure
    92	cp config/profile.example.yml config/profile.yml  # Edit with your details
    93	cp templates/portals.example.yml portals.yml       # Customize companies
    94	
    95	# 4. Add your CV
    96	# Create cv.md in the project root with your CV in markdown
    97	
    98	# 5. Personalize with Claude
    99	claude   # Open Claude Code in this directory
   100	
   101	# Then ask Claude to adapt the system to you:
   102	# "Change the archetypes to backend engineering roles"
   103	# "Translate the modes to English"
   104	# "Add these 5 companies to portals.yml"
   105	# "Update my profile with this CV I'm pasting"
   106	
   107	# 6. Start using
   108	# Paste a job URL or run /career-ops
   109	```
   110	
   111	> **The system is designed to be customized by Claude itself.** Modes, archetypes, scoring weights, negotiation scripts -- just ask Claude to change them. It reads the same files it uses, so it knows exactly what to edit.
   112	
   113	See [docs/SETUP.md](docs/SETUP.md) for the full setup guide.
   114	
   115	## Gemini CLI Integration
   116	
   117	Career-ops supports [Gemini CLI](https://github.com/google-gemini/gemini-cli) natively — the same way it supports Claude Code and OpenCode. All 15 slash commands are available, using the same `modes/*.md` evaluation logic.
   118	
   119	### Option A — Native Gemini CLI (Recommended)
   120	
   121	```bash
   122	# 1. Install Gemini CLI
   123	npm install -g @google/gemini-cli
   124	# or: npx @google/gemini-cli --version
   125	
   126	# 2. Authenticate (free — uses your Google account)
   127	gemini auth
   128	
   129	# 3. Run in the career-ops directory
   130	cd career-ops
   131	gemini
   132	
   133	# 4. Use slash commands just like Claude Code
   134	/career-ops "Senior AI Engineer at Anthropic..."
   135	/career-ops-evaluate --file ./jds/openai.txt
   136	/career-ops-scan
   137	/career-ops-pdf
   138	/career-ops-tracker
   139	```
   140	
   141	The `GEMINI.md` file is auto-loaded as context. All 15 commands are defined in `.gemini/commands/*.toml`.
   142	
   143	### Option B — Standalone API Script (No CLI install needed)
   144	
   145	```bash
   146	# 1. Get a free API key at https://aistudio.google.com/apikey
   147	cp .env.example .env
   148	# Edit .env → set GEMINI_API_KEY=your_key_here
   149	
   150	# 2. Install dependencies
   151	npm install
   152	
   153	# 3. Evaluate a job description
   154	node gemini-eval.mjs "We are looking for a Senior AI Engineer..."
   155	node gemini-eval.mjs --file ./jds/my-job.txt
   156	npm run gemini:eval -- "JD text here"
   157	```
   158	
   159	> **Free tier:** Both options work without billing. Native CLI uses Google OAuth; the API script uses `gemini-2.0-flash` (15 RPM, 1M tokens/day free).
	< truncated lines 160-168 >
   169	/career-ops pdf            → Generate ATS-optimized CV
   170	/career-ops batch          → Batch evaluate multiple offers
   171	/career-ops tracker        → View application status
   172	/career-ops apply          → Fill application forms with AI
   173	/career-ops pipeline       → Process pending URLs
   174	/career-ops contacto       → LinkedIn outreach message
   175	/career-ops deep           → Deep company research
   176	/career-ops training       → Evaluate a course/cert
   177	/career-ops project        → Evaluate a portfolio project
   178	```
   179	
   180	Or just paste a job URL or description directly -- career-ops auto-detects it and runs the full pipeline.
   181	
   182	## How It Works
   183	
   184	```
   185	You paste a job URL or description
   186	        │
   187	        ▼
   188	┌──────────────────┐
   189	│  Archetype       │  Classifies: LLMOps / Agentic / PM / SA / FDE / Transformation
   190	│  Detection       │
   191	└────────┬─────────┘
   192	         │
   193	┌────────▼─────────┐
   194	│  A-F Evaluation  │  Match, gaps, comp research, STAR stories
   195	│  (reads cv.md)   │
   196	└────────┬─────────┘
   197	         │
   198	    ┌────┼────┐
   199	    ▼    ▼    ▼
   200	 Report  PDF  Tracker
   201	  .md   .pdf   .tsv
   202	```
   203	
   204	## Pre-configured Portals
   205	
   206	The scanner comes with **45+ companies** ready to scan and **19 search queries** across major job boards. Copy `templates/portals.example.yml` to `portals.yml` and add your own:
   207	
   208	**AI Labs:** Anthropic, OpenAI, Mistral, Cohere, LangChain, Pinecone
   209	**Voice AI:** ElevenLabs, PolyAI, Parloa, Hume AI, Deepgram, Vapi, Bland AI
   210	**AI Platforms:** Retool, Airtable, Vercel, Temporal, Glean, Arize AI
   211	**Contact Center:** Ada, LivePerson, Sierra, Decagon, Talkdesk, Genesys
   212	**Enterprise:** Salesforce, Twilio, Gong, Dialpad
   213	**LLMOps:** Langfuse, Weights & Biases, Lindy, Cognigy, Speechmatics
   214	**Automation:** n8n, Zapier, Make.com
   215	**European:** Factorial, Attio, Tinybird, Clarity AI, Travelperk
   216	
   217	**Job boards searched:** Ashby, Greenhouse, Lever, Wellfound, Workable, RemoteFront
   218	
   219	## Dashboard TUI
   220	
   221	The built-in terminal dashboard lets you browse your pipeline visually:
   222	
   223	```bash
   224	cd dashboard
   225	go build -o career-dashboard .
   226	./career-dashboard --path ..
   227	```
   228	
   229	Features: 6 filter tabs, 4 sort modes, grouped/flat view, lazy-loaded previews, inline status changes.
   230	
   231	## Project Structure
   232	
   233	```
   234	career-ops/
   235	├── CLAUDE.md                    # Agent instructions
   236	├── cv.md                        # Your CV (create this)
   237	├── article-digest.md            # Your proof points (optional)
   238	├── config/
   239	│   └── profile.example.yml      # Template for your profile
   240	├── modes/                       # 14 skill modes
   241	│   ├── _shared.md               # Shared context (customize this)
   242	│   ├── oferta.md                # Single evaluation
   243	│   ├── pdf.md                   # PDF generation
   244	│   ├── scan.md                  # Portal scanner
   245	│   ├── batch.md                 # Batch processing
   246	│   └── ...
   247	├── templates/
   248	│   ├── cv-template.html         # ATS-optimized CV template
   249	│   ├── portals.example.yml      # Scanner config template
   250	│   └── states.yml               # Canonical statuses
   251	├── batch/
   252	│   ├── batch-prompt.md          # Self-contained worker prompt
   253	│   └── batch-runner.sh          # Orchestrator script
   254	├── dashboard/                   # Go TUI pipeline viewer
   255	├── data/                        # Your tracking data (gitignored)
   256	├── reports/                     # Evaluation reports (gitignored)
   257	├── output/                      # Generated PDFs (gitignored)
   258	├── fonts/                       # Space Grotesk + DM Sans
   259	├── docs/                        # Setup, customization, architecture
   260	└── examples/                    # Sample CV, report, proof points
   261	```
   262	
   263	## Tech Stack
   264	
   265	![Claude Code](https://img.shields.io/badge/Claude_Code-000?style=flat&logo=anthropic&logoColor=white)
   266	![Node.js](https://img.shields.io/badge/Node.js-339933?style=flat&logo=node.js&logoColor=white)
   267	![Playwright](https://img.shields.io/badge/Playwright-2EAD33?style=flat&logo=playwright&logoColor=white)
   268	![Go](https://img.shields.io/badge/Go-00ADD8?style=flat&logo=go&logoColor=white)
   269	![Bubble Tea](https://img.shields.io/badge/Bubble_Tea-FF75B5?style=flat&logo=go&logoColor=white)
   270	
   271	- **Agent**: Claude Code with custom skills and modes
   272	- **PDF**: Playwright/Puppeteer + HTML template
   273	- **Scanner**: Playwright + Greenhouse API + WebSearch
   274	- **Dashboard**: Go + Bubble Tea + Lipgloss (Catppuccin Mocha theme)
   275	- **Data**: Markdown tables + YAML config + TSV batch files
   276

   297	## Disclaimer
   298	
   299	**career-ops is a local, open-source tool — NOT a hosted service.** By using this software, you acknowledge:
   300	
   301	1. **You control your data.** Your CV, contact info, and personal data stay on your machine and are sent directly to the AI provider you choose (Anthropic, OpenAI, etc.). We do not collect, store, or have access to any of your data.
   302	2. **You control the AI.** The default prompts instruct the AI not to auto-submit applications, but AI models can behave unpredictably. If you modify the prompts or use different models, you do so at your own risk. **Always review AI-generated content for accuracy before submitting.**
   303	3. **You comply with third-party ToS.** You must use this tool in accordance with the Terms of Service of the career portals you interact with (Greenhouse, Lever, Workday, LinkedIn, etc.). Do not use this tool to spam employers or overwhelm ATS systems.
   304	4. **No guarantees.** Evaluations are recommendations, not truth. AI models may hallucinate skills or experience. The authors are not liable for employment outcomes, rejected applications, account restrictions, or any other consequences.
   305	
   306	See [LEGAL_DISCLAIMER.md](LEGAL_DISCLAIMER.md) for full details. This software is provided under the [MIT License](LICENSE) "as is", without warranty of any kind.

Packet
     2	
     3	A single-file Streamlit app that:
     4	- Parses uploaded resumes (PDF/DOCX/TXT/URLs) and **autofills** a construction-facing resume form.
     5	- Maps **detected past roles** to duty **bullets** from `Job_History_Master.docx`. Clicking bullets also **infers skills**.
     6	- Exports a **DOCX resume** via `docxtpl` using `resume_app_template.docx`.
     7	- Generates a **Cover Letter** (DOCX) with crew-forward, measurable language.
     8	- Builds an **Instructor Pathway Packet** (DOCX) embedding student reflections, full text of uploads, and the selected trade’s section from `Stand_Out_Playbook_Master.docx`.
     9	
    10	## Quick Start
    11	
    12	### Installation
    13	
    14	1. Ensure Python 3.11+ is installed
    15	2. Install dependencies:
    16	   ```bash
    17	   pip install -r requirements.txt
    18	   ```
    19	
    20	### Running the App
    21	
    22	```bash
    23	streamlit run app.py
    24	```
    25	
    26	The app will open in your browser at `http://localhost:8501`
    27	
    28	### Verification
    29	
    30	To verify everything is working correctly, run the verification test suite:
    31	
    32	```bash
    33	python3 test_verification.py
    34	```
    35	
    36	This will test:
    37	- ✓ All Python dependencies are installed
    38	- ✓ Required data files are present
    39	- ✓ Text parsing functions work correctly
    40	- ✓ Job Master DOCX parsing works
    41	- ✓ Document generation (Resume, Cover Letter, Pathway Packet) works
    42	- ✓ Utility functions work correctly
    43	
    44	## Repo layout
    45	     1	# Content Specification for Resume Workshop App
     2	
     3	## Overview
     4	This document describes the structure, format, and purpose of all content files used in the Seattle Tri-County Construction Resume & Pathway Packet application.
     5	
     6	## File Inventory
     7	
     8	### Core Content Files
     9	
    10	1. **CONTENT_MASTER.md** - The comprehensive master content document containing all trade-specific guidance, objectives, bullets, skills, and artifact templates.
    11	
    12	2. **Resume_Context_Schema.json** - JSON schema defining the structure of resume data.
    13	
    14	3. **Objective_Starters_Bank.json** - JSON-formatted objectives organized by trade (apprenticeship and job).
    15	
    16	4. **Objective_Starters_By_Trade.csv** - CSV format of objectives for easy filtering and import.
    17	
    18	5. **Role_Bullets_Master.md** - Markdown document with duty bullets per detected role (≤24 words, measured/evidence-ready).
    19	
    20	6. **Skills_Canon.json** - JSON file with skills organized into three buckets: Transferable, Job-Specific, and Self-Management.
    21	
    22	7. **Certification_Normalization.csv** - CSV mapping various certification names to standardized resume phrases.
    23	
    24	8. **Credential_MicroBadges_Library.md** - Trade-specific micro-credentials with resume phrases and proof artifact requirements.
    25	
    26	9. **Prep_Metrics_Library.md** - Named drills and how they're recorded (timed carry, conduit bending, etc.).
    27	
    28	10. **Proof_Artifact_Templates.md** - Text templates for checklists, logs, and verification forms.
    29	
    30	### Tracking Templates
    31	
    32	11. **Artifact_Tracker_Template.csv** - Blank CSV template for tracking proof artifacts (Item, Source, Date, Expiry, File/Link, Verifier, Notes).
    33	
    34	12. **Mobility_Plan_Sources_Template.csv** - Template for logging multi-state application sources and calendars.
    35	
    36	13. **Social_Intel_Queue_Template.csv** - Template for tracking trade-specific insights and evidence requirements.
    37	
    38	### Supporting Documents
    39	
    40	14. **Cross_Trade_Entry_Tests_Appendix.md** - Summary of entry tests, physicals, and prep resources across trades.
    41	
    42	15. **Pathway_Packet_Structure.md** - Document describing the structure and sections of the Pathway Packet output.
    43	
    44	16. **How_to_embed_in_app.md** - Integration guide for embedding content files into app workflows.
    45	
    46	17. **Stand_Out_Playbook_Master_APPEND_ONLY_Scaffold.md** - Scaffold structure for the trade-specific Stand-Out Playbook with append-only "Do Next" sections.
    47	
    48	18. **One_Page_Resume_Layout.txt** - Plain text layout showing the exact structure of a one-page resume.
    49	
    50	19. **Trade_List.txt** - Simple line-separated list of all supported trades.
    51	
    52	20. **Detected_Roles_Index.csv** - Index mapping common job titles to standardized role names used in bullet bank.
    53	
    54	21. **Resume_Field_Hints.md** - Guidance and hints for filling out each resume field (Objective, Experience, Skills, Certifications, Education).
    55	
    56	22. **Packet_Checklists_Blank.md** - Blank checklists for 0-2 weeks, 2-6 weeks, and 6-12 weeks action items.
    57	
    58	## Content Principles
    59	
    60	### Evidence Doctrine
    61	"If you can't attach it (card, score, log, checklist, sign-off, face-free photo), it's weak."
    62	
    63	### Neutrality Guardrails
    64	- Forbidden terms: "union," "non-union," local numbers in objectives
    65	- Use neutral, factual, crew-useful language
    66	- No sub-trade labels in objectives
    67	
    68	### Measurement Standard
    69	- Bullets: ≤24 words, with measured/evidence-ready phrasing
    70	- Resume: One page, ≤12 total skills, 3-4 measured bullets per job
    71	- Objectives: Neutral wording, chosen from starter bank or edited by student
    72	
    73	### Privacy Requirements
    74	- Photos must exclude faces and sensitive site identifiers
    75	- No personal data in templates
    76	- Permission documented when identifiable content is necessary
    77	
    78	## Data Formats
    79	
    80	### JSON Files
    81	- Use consistent structure with clear hierarchies
    82	- Include validation-friendly field names
    83	- Support both apprenticeship and job categories where applicable
    84	
    85	### CSV Files
    86	- Include header row
    87	- Use consistent column ordering
    88	- Quote fields containing commas or newlines
    89	- UTF-8 encoding
    90	
    91	### Markdown Files
    92	- Use consistent heading hierarchy
    93	- Include clear section markers
    94	- Format bullets consistently
    95	- Maintain ≤24 word limit for duty bullets
    96	
    97	### Plain Text Files
    98	- UTF-8 encoding
    99	- Line-separated for list files
   100	- Clear structure for layout templates
   101	
   102	## Integration Notes
   103	
   104	All content files are designed to:
   105	1. Support offline-first architecture (bundled in app)
   106	2. Enable dynamic loading without code changes
   107	3. Maintain a single source of truth for trade-specific content
   108	4. Allow easy updates by instructors and content managers
   109	5. Support validation and verification workflows
   110	
   111	## Versioning
   112	Content files should be versioned alongside the application. Breaking changes to structure require corresponding app updates.
   113	
   114	## Contact
   115	For questions about content structure or updates, refer to How_to_embed_in_app.md.
   116	     1	# PR Summary: Integrate CONTENT_MASTER.md for Dynamic Content Loading
     2	
     3	## Overview
     4	This PR successfully integrates CONTENT_MASTER.md into the Flutter mobile app, enabling dynamic loading of trade-specific objectives, skills, certifications, and artifact templates. The app is now fully configurable through a single markdown file, eliminating all hardcoded trade-specific data.
     5

    10	2. ✅ Data models for all content types
    11	3. ✅ State management with error handling

    13	5. ✅ Loading states and error feedback
    14	6. ✅ Fallback mechanisms for stability
    15	7. ✅ Unit tests for models and parsing
    16	8. ✅ Comprehensive documentation
    17	9. ✅ Verification checklist for testing

    44

    46	   - Loading progress
    47	   - Success status with counts
    48	   - Error messages with fallback
    49	
    50	### Error Handling
    51	- Service level: Returns empty content on failure
    52	- Parser level: Catches errors, logs, returns empty collections
    53	- Provider level: Exposes error messages
    54	- UI level: Shows loading/error/success states

   142	Perfect! Now I understand what you're working on. Let me create a summary and ask you some clarifying questions:

## What I See

**Career-Ops** (the reference project):
- A sophisticated AI-powered job search system
- Evaluates job postings with structured scoring (A-F)
- Generates tailored PDFs/resumes per job description
- Portal scanner that navigates career pages automatically
- Batch processing for multiple jobs
- Built for white-collar/tech job searches (software engineering, AI roles, etc.)
- Uses Claude Code/Gemini CLI with custom "modes" (evaluation prompts)
- Tracks everything in markdown/TSV files
- Has a Go-based terminal dashboard

**Your Resume Workshop App**:
- Construction-focused resume builder for pre-apprenticeship students
- Streamlit app that parses uploaded resumes
- Maps past roles to trade-specific duty bullets
- Exports DOCX resumes + cover letters + pathway packets
- Has a Flutter mobile app component
- Content-driven (CONTENT_MASTER.md with trade-specific guidance)
- Evidence-based approach (proof artifacts, certifications, measured bullets)
- Built for ANEW students entering skilled trades

## What You're Envisioning

A **Construction-Focused Career-Ops System** that combines:
- The automation & AI evaluation power of Career-Ops
- The construction-specific content & evidence framework from your Resume Workshop
- Targeted for pre-apprenticeship students and women entering the trades

## Questions Before We Start Building:

1. **Primary User**: Who is the main user - ANEW instructors helping students, or students themselves using it directly?

2. **Core Use Case**: What's the #1 thing this should do?
   - Help students find and apply to apprenticeships?
   - Help students build construction-focused resumes for specific job postings?
   - Track apprenticeship applications across different trades/locals?
   - Something else?

3. **Job Sources**: Where do construction jobs/apprenticeships get posted?
   - Union hall websites?
   - Specific portals (like how Career-Ops has Greenhouse/Lever)?
   - Company career pages?
   - Government sites (apprenticeship.gov)?

4. **Evaluation Criteria**: What makes a "good match" for a construction apprenticeship?
   - Physical requirements met?
   - Geographic proximity?
   - Trade preference alignment?
   - Entry requirements (test scores, certifications)?

5. **Output Format**: What should it produce?
   - Construction-optimized resumes (like your current app)?
   - Cover letters?
   - Application tracking?
   - Interview prep materials?

Once I understand your vision better, we can build this step by step, starting with the highest-value feature first.

**[USER]**

okay so this is the thing. 1. it will need to be live so it can do live searches. we search for entry level hold over jobs for our students. there are two goals for live searches. 1. help students find work. 2 generate partners. 1. we also need to filter out the bad apples for the students. there are some shitty companies out there. also i would like to be able to use the L&I webpage look up a contract to run a report on that contractor and get a score on that contract. i do not want to use API keys, our students come from very poor areas, we are helping students who dont have access get access to a job market that does not make space for them. we work with students that are super low income and my company is a non profit. so i need to make this as free as i can for them. maybe later i can find contractors to buy in. then if you look in my google drive you will see a bunch of work i have done with hold over jobs, resume help. construction focused resumes, resume language. how to take different careers and rewrite your resume to be applicable to construction language. we help write cover letters.

**[ASSISTANT]**

Got it. This is a **student-facing job search & application system** for construction holdover work with contractor vetting built in. Let me break down what I'm hearing:

## Core Features You Need

### 1. **Live Job Search** (No API keys)
- Search for entry-level construction holdover jobs
- Two purposes: student employment + identifying potential ANEW partners
- Need to filter OUT bad contractors automatically

### 2. **Contractor Vetting via L&I**
- Scrape/lookup WA State L&I contractor data
- Generate a "safety score" for each contractor
- Protect students from exploitative companies

### 3. **Resume Translation Engine**
- Take ANY career background → rewrite in construction language
- Construction-specific resume optimization
- Cover letter generation with construction terminology

### 4. **Google Drive Integration**
- You already have content/examples in Drive
- Pull from your existing holdover job research
- Use your resume language guides

## Technical Approach (Keeping it FREE)

Since you want **no API keys** and need **live searches**, here's what we can do:

**Option A: Browser Automation (Best for you)**
- Use the career-ops approach with Playwright
- Navigate job sites directly (Indeed, Craigslist, company pages)
- Scrape L&I contractor lookup pages
- **Cost**: $0 (just runs on your computer or a student's computer)
- **Downside**: Slower, requires the app to be running locally

**Option B: Hybrid (My recommendation)**
- Use Claude.ai (you're already here, it's free for basic use)
- Students paste job postings into the system
- System evaluates + rewrites resume + vets contractor
- Google Drive MCP for your content library
- **Cost**: $0 for students, works in browser
- **Upside**: No installation, accessible anywhere

## Questions to Lock Down the MVP:

1. **Where do students find jobs NOW?** 
   - Indeed? Craigslist? Facebook? Company websites? Union halls?
   - Which 2-3 sources should we prioritize?

2. **L&I Contractor Lookup** - Can you show me:
   - The exact L&I page you use to look up contractors?
   - What data points matter? (violations, safety records, wage theft, bonding?)

3. **Your Google Drive Content** - What's already there?
   - Resume examples by source career → construction?
   - Holdover job descriptions you've collected?
   - Cover letter templates?

4. **Student Access** - How do students use tools now?
   - Do they have laptops? Or mostly phones?
   - Are they comfortable with terminal/command line, or need a web interface?

5. **Immediate Need** - What's the #1 most time-consuming thing YOU do right now that we could automate first?
   - Searching for jobs manually?
   - Vetting contractors one by one?
   - Rewriting resumes for students?
   - Writing cover letters?

Let me know and I'll start building the first working piece today. We can iterate from there.

**[USER]**

is there a free open source AI that we could use?

**[ASSISTANT]**

Yes! Several excellent options for a free, open-source AI system:

## Best Options for Your Use Case

### 1. **Ollama (My Top Recommendation for You)**
- **What it is**: Runs AI models locally on any computer
- **Cost**: 100% FREE, no API keys ever
- **Models**: Llama 3.3 (70B), Qwen, DeepSeek, Mistral
- **Privacy**: Everything stays local, perfect for student data
- **Hardware**: Works on normal laptops (even older ones with smaller models)
- **Setup**: Super easy - download and run

```bash
# Install Ollama
curl -fsSL https://ollama.com/install.sh | sh

# Download a model (one-time, ~4GB)
ollama pull llama3.2

# Use it in your app (no API keys needed)
ollama run llama3.2
```

**Why this is perfect for you:**
- Students can run it on their own computers (even offline)
- No costs, no API limits, no tracking
- Can be packaged into a simple app they download once
- Works with Python/Node.js easily

### 2. **LM Studio** (Alternative - GUI version)
- Same concept as Ollama but with a nice interface
- Students can literally click and use it
- Great for non-technical users
- Free desktop app

### 3. **Hugging Face Inference API** (Free tier)
- Cloud-based but has generous free tier
- No credit card needed to start
- Access to many open models
- Good for web apps

### 4. **DeepSeek (NEW - Very Powerful)**
- Recent Chinese model that rivals GPT-4
- Can run via Ollama
- Excellent at reasoning and code
- Completely free

## My Recommendation for Your Project

**Start with Ollama + a simple web interface:**

```

    ↓
Ollama (running locally with Llama 3.3)
    ↓
Your Python/Node.js App
    ↓

**Why this stack:**
- ✅ $0 forever
- ✅ Student data never leaves their computer
- ✅ Works offline after initial model download

## Solution: Serverless + Free-Tier Cloud AI

**What if we build it as a 100% web app that runs on FREE cloud infrastructure?**

### Stack That Costs $0 Forever:

1. **Frontend**: Static website (GitHub Pages or Vercel - FREE)
2. **Backend**: Cloudflare Workers (FREE tier: 100k requests/day)
3. **AI**: Hugging Face Inference API (FREE tier, no credit card)
4. **Storage**: Cloudflare KV or Supabase (FREE tier)
5. **Web Scraping**: Cloudflare Workers + Playwright (runs in the cloud)

**Result**: 
- Students type a URL in ANY browser (library, case manager's laptop, jail computer lab)
- Everything happens in the cloud
- No downloads, no installs, no API keys for students
- Just works at: `anew-career-help.app` or whatever domain

### How It Works:

```
Student on ANY device with internet
    ↓
Opens: anew-career-help.app
    ↓
Pastes job URL or contractor name
    ↓
Cloud worker:
  - Scrapes the job posting
  - Looks up contractor on L&I
  - Runs AI analysis (Hugging Face free tier)
  - Generates resume + cover letter
    ↓
Student downloads PDF or copies text
```

### Free Tier Limits That Actually Work:

**Hugging Face Inference API:**
- FREE forever (no credit card)
- ~1000 requests/day per model
- Can rotate between models if needed
- Good models: Llama 3.2, Mistral, Qwen

**Cloudflare Workers:**
- 100,000 requests/day FREE
- Enough for 1000+ students/day
- Runs serverless (no server to maintain)

**Vercel/Netlify:**
- FREE hosting for the website
- Global CDN (fast everywhere)
- Easy deploys from GitHub

### Alternative: Fully Client-Side (Even Better?)

Build it so the AI runs IN THE BROWSER using WebLLM:

```
Student opens website
    ↓
Browser downloads small AI model (~500MB, one-time)
    ↓
Everything runs locally in the browser
    ↓
Even works offline after first load
```

**Tools:**
- **WebLLM** - runs Llama in the browser
- **Transformers.js** - Hugging Face models in browser
- Works on library computers (downloads to browser cache)

### The Most Accessible Option: Progressive Web App (PWA)

What if we build it as a PWA that:
- Works in any browser (no app store)
- Can be "installed" by adding to home screen (no real install)
- Works offline after first use
- Saves work locally (survives closing browser)

## The Real Problem You're Solving:

**Students who are:**
- On probation/parole with internet restrictions
- In work release programs
- Under supervision that limits web access
- BUT they CAN use approved educational/employment apps

**The Solution:**
A **sandboxed, approved app** that:
- Searches the internet FOR them (backend does the scraping)
- Shows curated, vetted results (no direct internet access)
- Generates application materials (resume, cover letter)
- Logs everything for case managers/compliance
- Students never "browse the web" - they just use the app

## This Changes Everything

Now I understand why it MUST be an app, not a website. It's:
- ✅ Approvable by corrections/parole officers
- ✅ Auditable (logs what they search/access)
- ✅ Controlled (they can't browse Indeed, they search "electrician" in YOUR app)
- ✅ Evidence-based (proves they're job searching, not web browsing)

```
Student's Device (Supervised/Restricted)
    ↓

    ↓

    ↓

## The Flow:

1. **Daily Background Job** (automated):
   - Scrapes Indeed/Craigslist for "entry level electrician Seattle"
   - Looks up each contractor on L&I
   - Scores companies (safety violations, wage theft, etc.)
   - Filters out bad ones
   - Stores vetted jobs in database

2. **Student Opens App**:
   - Types: "electrician"
   - Sees: Pre-vetted, ranked jobs (updated daily)
   - No direct internet access needed

3. **Student Applies**:
   - App asks for their background (retail → construction translation)
   - Generates construction-focused resume
   - Generates cover letter
   - Creates PDF
   - Logs application for case manager

4. **Case Manager Portal**:
   - Sees what students searched
   - Sees what jobs they applied to
   - Can verify they're job searching (for compliance)
   - Can help guide them

    38	Instructor Packet — “Stand Out” Playbook (Seattle tri-county focus)
    39	Updated: October 14, 2025
    40	
    41	Context
    42	Pre-apprentice grads already have Flagger, OSHA-10, and Forklift. This playbook lists beyond-baseline moves that measurably improve selection odds for union and non-union pathways in King, Pierce, and Snohomish counties. Keep objectives neutral (no union/non-union or sub-trade labels).
    43	
    44	Verify the basics (what they really mean)
    45	• OSHA-10/30: Outreach training cards, not “certifications.” OSHA-30 is typically for leads/supervisors. Some owners/GCs require Outreach; cite it correctly (e.g., “OSHA Outreach 10-Hour (Construction)”).
    46	• Forklift: Employers must train/evaluate/certify on the specific truck(s) and workplace; evaluation at least every 3 years. Third-party classes help, but on-site employer evaluation is what counts.
    47	• WA Flagger: Training must meet WAC; card expiration is max 3 years from issuance and requires photo ID.
    48	• Rule of thumb: Show evidence (dates, evaluator, equipment class) rather than vague claims.
    49	
    50	Quick wins by target
    51	
    52	Electrical (Inside, Residential, Limited Energy)
    53	Program reality check (union): Inside Wire apprenticeship ~8,000 OJT + ~1,000 classroom hours before WA (01) exam. Expect algebra and steady attendance.
    54	Stand-out stack:
    55	  – Documented tool time: conduit measuring, simple bends, layout, wire pulls, labeling/testing, terminations (supervised).
    56	  – Low-voltage crossover: labeling, continuity testing, device counts, as-built updates.
    57	  – Holdover jobs: warehouse/runner at ECs, prefab shop, material handler.
    58	Evidence bullets:
    59	  – “Measured and marked 20+ EMT runs (½–1 in.), verified offsets with level; staged hardware by circuit.”
    60	  – “Assisted two-person pulls; maintained lube, pulling tension calls, and device labeling.”
    61	Study cues to log:
    62	  – Code vocabulary (lockout/tagout basics, conductor IDs), print reading (symbols, schedules), torque/termination habits.
    63	
    64	Pipe Trades / HVAC-R (Plumber, Steamfitter, HVAC-R)
    65	Program reality check: Multiple programs with classroom + OJT; math, brazing/soldering foundations, and safe handling are emphasized.
    66	Stand-out stack:
    67	  – EPA 608 (Type I/II/III or Universal); durable credential—list the Type explicitly on resume.
    68	  – Shop helper/parts counter; sheet-metal fab helper; maintenance tech trainee.
    69	Evidence bullets:

[1036 lines total]Perfect. Now I see it. You built a **resume transformation engine** but hit the wall when real-world constraints showed up:
- Students can't access the app easily
- Students can't safely browse job sites
- Students need jobs vetted BEFORE they see them
- Students need the system to work WITHOUT requiring devices

Now let me name this right.

---

## **TradeGate**

**Why this name:**
- **Trade** = skilled construction trades (electrician, plumber, carpenter, etc.)
- **Gate** = controlled entry point (you control what jobs pass through)
- **Gate** = opens doors (to employment, to opportunity)
- **Gate** = barrier protection (keeps bad contractors OUT)

**Tagline:** *The job search system that protects you before you apply.*

---

## What TradeGate Does

**For Students:**
- Type "electrician" → Get 10 VETTED entry-level jobs
- Click a job → Get construction-focused resume + cover letter
- Never touch the open internet (compliance-safe)
- Works on supervised/restricted devices

**For You (and future employers/case managers):**
- Daily automated job scraping (Indeed, Craigslist, etc.)
- L&I contractor verification (filters out bad employers)
- Resume translation engine (retail → construction language)
- Application tracking (for compliance/proof of job search)
- Partner pipeline (good contractors become placement partners)

**The Secret Sauce:**
Your CONTENT_MASTER framework embedded as the AI's training:
- Evidence-based bullets (measured, specific, ≤24 words)
- Neutral language (no union/non-union)
- Trade-specific resume optimization
- Your proven holdover job strategies

---

## The Build Plan (MVP First)

### Phase 1: Core Job Search Engine (2 weeks)
**What it does:**
- Backend scraper runs daily (Indeed + Craigslist for now)
- Searches: "entry level [electrician/laborer/carpenter] Seattle"
- Stores jobs in free database (Supabase)
- Simple mobile app: student types trade → sees job list

**Tech:**
- Flutter app (works on any device, can be corrections-approved)
- Supabase backend (FREE tier: unlimited API requests, 500MB DB)
- Python scraper (runs on Railway FREE tier)
- No AI yet (just search + display)

### Phase 2: L&I Contractor Vetting (1 week)
**What it does:**
- For each job, extracts company name
- Looks up on WA L&I contractor database
- Checks: violations, wage theft, bonding, safety record
- Scores 0-100 (filters out <60)

**I need from you:**
- Show me the L&I lookup page you use
- What red flags matter most?

### Phase 3: Resume Generation (1 week)
**What it does:**
- Student enters current job (e.g., "McDonald's cashier")
- AI translates using YOUR frameworks:
  - "Maintained clean workspace" → "Maintained clear egress and staging zones per safety plan"
  - "Handled inventory" → "Tracked parts and hardware; verified counts against manifest"
- Generates one-page DOCX resume
- Generates cover letter

**Tech:**
- Hugging Face FREE API (Llama 3.2)
- Your CONTENT_MASTER as the system prompt
- All your Drive content as examples

### Phase 4: Application Tracking (1 week)
**What it does:**
- Logs every job student views
- Logs every application generated
- Case manager portal to verify job search activity
- Compliance reports for parole/work release

---

## Immediate Next Steps

1. **You create the Google Drive folder** with:
   - Your holdover job research
   - Resume translation examples (retail→construction, etc.)
   - L&I contractor lookup process
   - Cover letter templates
   - Any other content I should embed

2. **I build the scraper proof-of-concept:**
   - Scrapes 10 "entry level electrician Seattle" jobs from Indeed
   - Shows you the raw data
   - We verify it's pulling the right stuff

3. **You show me L&I:**
   - Exact URL for contractor lookup
   - What data points you check
   - Example of a "good" vs "bad" contractor

4. **I'll create the TradeGate repo** with:
   - Flutter mobile app (empty shell for now)
   - Python backend (scraper + API)
   - Database schema
   - Deployment to free tiers

---

## Why I'm Invested

Because this is **exactly** the kind of problem that matters. You're not building another SaaS tool for people who already have privilege. You're building **infrastructure for justice** — for people the system forgot.

- Students with records who deserve second chances
- Women breaking into male-dominated trades  
- People without devices, without internet, without resources
- Students you're protecting from predatory employers

This is the work that counts.

**Let's build TradeGate.**

Ready when you are. Drop that Drive folder link and let's go.

<function>{"description": "Call this tool to search for Drive files given a structured query. The `query` field requires the use of query search operators. A query string contains the following three parts: `query_term operator values` where: - `query_term` is the query term or field to search upon. - `operator` specifies the condition for the query term. - `values` are the specific values to use to filter your search results. ## Query Terms The following table lists valid query terms with their descriptions: | Query Term | Valid operators | Usage | | ---------------- | ------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | | `title` | `contains`, `=`, `!=` | Title of the file. Surround with single quotes (`'`). Escape single quotes in queries with `\\'`, such as `'Valentine\\'s Day'`. | | `fullText` | `contains` | Whether the `title` or text in the file's content matches. Surround with single quotes (`'`). Escape single quotes in queries with `\\'`, such as `'Valentine\\'s Day'`. | | `mimeType` | `contains`, `=`, `!=` | MIME type of the file. Surround with single quotes (`'`). Escape single quotes in queries with `\\'`, such as `'Valentine\\'s Day'`. | | `modifiedTime` | `<=`, `<`, `=`, `!=`, `>`, `>=` | Date of the last file modification. RFC 3339 format, default time zone is UTC, such as `2012-06-04T12:00:00-08:00`. Fields of type `date` are not comparable. | | `viewedByMeTime` | `<=`, `<`, `=`, `!=`, `>`, `>=` | Date that the user last viewed a file. RFC 3339 format, default time zone is UTC, such as `2012-06-04T12:00:00-08:00`. Fields of type `date` are not comparable. | | `parentId` | `=`, `!=` | Whether the parent equals the specified ID. `root` can be used to specify the user's \"My Drive\" that functions as their primary hierarchy. | | `owner` | `=`, `!=` | User who owns the file. `me` can be used to specify the user that is making the request. | | `sharedWithMe` | `=`, `!=` | Files that are in the user's \"Shared with me\" collection. All file users are in the file's Access Control List (ACL). Can be either `true` or `false`. | | `createdTime` | `<=`, `<`, `=`, `!=`, `>`, `>=` | Date when the file was created. Use RFC 3339 format, default time zone is UTC, such as `2012-06-04T12:00:00-08:00`. | ## Query Operators The following table lists valid query operators: | Operator | Usage | | ---------- | ------------------------------------------------------------- | | `contains` | The content of one string is present in the other. | | `=` | The content of a string or boolean is equal to the other. | | `!=` | The content of a string or boolean is not equal to the other. | | `<` | A value is less than another. | | `<=` | A value is less than or equal to another. | | `>` | A value is greater than another. | | `>=` | A value is greater than or equal to another. | | `in` | An element is contained within a collection. | | `and` | Return items that match both queries. | | `or` | Return items that match either query. | | `not` | Negates a search query. | | `has` | A collection contains an element matching the parameters. | Some examples of queries include: - `title contains 'hello' and title contains 'goodbye'` - `modifiedTime > '2024-01-01T00:00:00Z' and (mimeType contains 'image/' or mimeType contains 'video/')` - `parentId = '1234567'` - `fullText contains 'hello'` - `owner = 'test@example.org'` - `sharedWithMe = true` - `owner = 'me'` (for files owned by the user)Utilize `next_page_token` to paginate through the results.       "parentId": "1Jwu6Ucffb3o-PRepV6hbuOmeQMYT6_tG",
      "contentSnippet": "Applying for Hold Over Jobs \n\n# Applying for “Hold-Over” Jobs While You Wait for Apprenticeship\n\n## 1\\. Why this matters\n\nIn Washington, there are thousands of active construction apprentices and more entering every year. Many of them are women and people of color entering through programs like ANEW and other pre-apprenticeships.[tradeswomenbuild.org](https://tradeswomenbuild.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/06/anew-paper-how-policy-and-collaboration-is-changing-the-face-of-construction-in-seattle-1.pdf)\n\nBut:\n\n  - Apprenticeship entry is competitive.  \n  - Most programs rank applicants and only pull from the top as work becomes available.  \n  - It can take months between interviews or “pulls” from the list.  \n  - The construction job market goes up and down. In the last year, Washington actually lost over 11,000 construction jobs, even though employers still report they need skilled workers.[KIRO 7 News Seattle  \n    ](https://www.kiro7.com/news/local/washington-construction-jobs-fall-short-amid-nationwide-growth/MUBBU244WZBOBLNNCRZVNJPF34/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou cannot control when you get called from an apprenticeship list.\n\nYou can control what you do in between.\n\nA “hold-over job” is a job you work while you are waiting for apprenticeship:\n\n  - It pays your bills.  \n  - It keeps you around tools, sites, and industry people.  \n  - It can build hours and experience that may help you later, if you do it correctly and legally.  \n\nThis lesson shows you how to:\n\n1.  Find hold-over jobs.  \n2.  Check if the employer is legal and safe.  \n3.  Understand electrical and plumbing trainee cards.  \n4.  Avoid fake “apprenticeships.”  \n5.  Use public training programs like BEAM or King County’s Operator-in-Training.  \n6.  Protect your hours, your body, and your rights.  \n\n-----\n\n## 2\\. Key terms (plain language)\n\n  - Hold-over job – A job you do in construction or a related field while you wait to enter your chosen apprenticeship.  \n  - Open shop / non-union – A contractor that is not signatory to a union. They can still be legal and legit, or they can be a complete mess. You have to check.  \n  - Registered apprenticeship – An apprenticeship program approved by the Washington State Apprenticeship and Training Council (through L\\&I) or the U.S. Department of Labor. This is what leads to a recognized journey card.[Apprenticeship.gov+1  \n    ](https://www.apprenticeship.gov/employers/registered-apprenticeship-program?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - Training agent – An employer approved to employ apprentices in a specific registered program. They show up under that program in the state’s apprenticeship system.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/apprenticeship-registration-and-tracking-system?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - Trainee card (electrical / plumbing) – A license from L\\&I that allows you to legally work as an electrical or plumbing trainee under supervision and log hours toward future licensing.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n  - Journey-level worker – Someone who has completed a registered apprenticeship or met the legal experience requirements and passed the state exam.[tradeswomenbuild.org+1  \n    ](https://tradeswomenbuild.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/06/anew-paper-how-policy-and-collaboration-is-changing-the-face-of-construction-in-seattle-1.pdf)\n\n-----\n\n## 3\\. Big picture: What a “good” hold-over job does for you\n\nA good hold-over job should:\n\n1.  Keep you close to your target trade (or at least the construction industry).  \n2.  Pay at or above legal minimum wage.  \n\n\u003c!-- end list --\u003e\n\n  - Washington state minimum wage in 2025 is $16.66/hour; some local cities (Seattle, Renton, Tukwila, SeaTac, unincorporated King County) have higher minimum wages over $20/hour.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/wages/minimum-wage/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n\u003c!-- end list --\u003e\n\n1.  Follow basic worker rights (rest breaks, overtime after 40 hours/week, workers’ comp coverage).[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/workplace-policies/rest-breaks-meal-periods-and-schedules?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n2.  Not require you to break the law (for example, doing electrical work without a trainee card).  \n3.  Ideally, build usable experience and certifications (hours, OSHA-10, forklift, flagger, etc.).  \n\nA bad hold-over job:\n\n  - Pays below legal minimum.  \n  - Pushes you to work as a “1099” contractor just to dodge taxes and workers’ comp.  \n  - Skips rest breaks, overtime pay, or safety gear.  \n  - Calls you an “apprentice” but is not a registered apprenticeship.  \n  - Has no L\\&I contractor registration or a history of serious violations.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov...",

(Key: Look for career/stability, not just \"hands-on.\")\n  - What is a successful apprentice? (Key: Reliable, coachable, safety-minded, drug-free.)\n  - What is the difference between pre-apprenticeship and apprenticeship? (Key: Prep vs. paid employment/classes.)\n  - Why did you choose pre-apprenticeship instead of applying straight to apprenticeship? (Key: Need for math, certifications, or trade exposure.)\n  - What did your program actually teach you? (Key: Shop work, math, tools, behavior, certifications.)\n\n### While-You-Wait / Jump-Rank Questions\n\n  - While you are waiting, are you actually building rank or just waiting? (Key: Math study, CDL, BEAM, helper work.)\n  - How do you verify a contractor before saying yes? (Key: WA L\\&I verify tool—check status, bond, insurance.)\n  - What is the difference between a legal job and hours that actually count? (Key: Need WSATC-approved program and training agent.)\n  - What proof of momentum should you be able to show today? (Key: Application confirmations, transcripts, work logs, certs.)\n\n## TRADE MODULES: PER-TRADE DRILLS\n\n### TRADE: BOILERMAKERS (LOCAL 104 & 502)\n\n#### 1\\. Pre-Apprentice Questions\n\n  - What is the difference between Local 104 and 502? (Key: 104 is shop/shipyard; 502 is construction/pipelines.)\n  - What does Local 104 require for assessment?\n\n#### 2\\. Ranking Questions\n\n  - What are you doing to jump rank? (Key: Welding practice/certs, rigging familiarity.)\n\n#### 3\\. Union/Local Questions\n\n  - What are the ID and education requirements for Local 502? (Key: Diploma/GED, DL, Drug test.)\n\n#### 4\\. Non-Union Questions\n\n  - If you took non-union fabrication work, what would actually help you? (Key: Welding exposure, rigging awareness.)\n\n#### 5\\. City Options & Locations\n\n  - Local 104: Seattle; Local 502: Puyallup.\n\n#### 6\\. Scenario (Pressure Question)\n\nThe Confined Space: \"Boilermaker work often involves tight, dark, hot enclosures inside vessels. Tell me about a time you had to perform precision work while physically uncomfortable or in a restricted space.\"\n\n#### 7\\. Grading\n\nInstructor Notes: \\[\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\] Score: \\_\\_\\_\\_ / 5\n\n### TRADE: CARPENTERS (GENERAL, INTERIOR, MILLWRIGHT, PILE DRIVER)\n\n#### 1\\. Pre-Apprentice Questions\n\n  - Which carpentry craft are you aiming at?       "contentSnippet": "# Master Trade-Specific Mock Interview Instructor Guide\n\nThis document is designed for instructors to use during mock interview sessions. It is organized by trade so that all relevant questions, local requirements, and scenarios are accessible in one place. No original content has been removed; the material has been reorganized for maximum efficiency during live student interactions.\n\n## Global Instructor Scoring Rubric\n\nUse this 1–5 scale to grade each answer within the trade-specific sections.\n\n|  |  |  |\n| :-: | :-: | :-: |\n| Score | Performance Level | Expectation  |\n| 1 | Unprepared | Cannot answer; no knowledge of the trade or path; lacks eye contact. |\n| 2 | Vague | General answers (e.g., \"I like hands-on work\") without specifics. |\n| 3 | Competent | Understands basic requirements; shows genuine interest and effort. |\n| 4 | Trade-Ready | Can name the Local; has physical evidence (OSHA card, etc.); answers clearly. |\n| 5 | Highly Preferred | Provides \"Proof of Momentum\" (recent work/certifications); exceptional confidence. |\n\n-----\n\n## TRADE: CARPENTERS (NW CARPENTERS UNION)\n\n### 1\\. Pre-Apprentice Questions\n\n  - Why did you choose the Carpenters pre-apprenticeship program specifically?\n  - Tell me about your experience working with wood or concrete forms during your training.\n\n### 2\\. Ranking Questions\n\n  - On a scale of 1-10, rate your ability to accurately read a tape measure to the 1/16th.\n  - How many hours of shop time have you logged in the last 30 days?\n\n### 3\\. Union/Local Questions (Local 30, 41, 129, etc.)\n\n  - What is the significance of obtaining an \"Intent to Hire\" letter in the Carpenters union?\n  - Are you aware of the dues structure and the requirement to maintain \"good standing\" during your apprenticeship?\n\n### 4\\. Non-Union Questions\n\n  - Are you willing to work for a non-signatory residential contractor while waiting for a union dispatch?\n  - Do you have your own basic set of hand tools (belt, hammer, speed square, tape)?\n\n### 5\\. City Options & Locations\n\n  - Training Centers: Kent, WA; Dupont, WA; Renton, WA.\n  - \"Are you willing to travel to job sites in Pierce, King, and Snohomish counties?\"\n\n### 6\\. Scenario (Pressure Question)\n\nThe Plumb Line Test: \"You’ve just finished framing a 10-foot wall. You check it and realize it is 3/4 of an inch out of plumb. Your Journeyman is already calling for the next plate. Do you hide the mistake or stop the flow to fix it?\"\n\n### 7\\. Grading (Section Total)\n\nInstructor Notes: \\[\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\] Score: \\_\\_\\_\\_ / 30\n\n-----\n\n## TRADE: ELECTRICIANS (IBEW LOCAL 46)\n\n### 1\\. Pre-Apprentice Questions\n\n  - Do you have your official high school transcripts showing successful completion of Algebra 1?\n  - Why does the electrical trade interest you more than a general labor trade?\n\n### 2\\. Ranking Questions\n\n  - Describe your level of comfort working with color-coded systems and small components.\n  - How do you handle repetitive tasks that require high precision for 8+ hours?\n\n### 3\\. Union/Local Questions (Local 46)\n\n  - Do you understand the difference between Inside Wireman, Limited Energy, and Residential classifications?\n  - What is the current \"Rank\" or \"Zone\" system for the Local 46 waiting list?\n\n### 4\\. Non-Union Questions\n\n  - If a private electrical contractor offers you a trainee position, will you accept it to gain hours toward your 01 license?\n\n### 5\\. City Options & Locations\n\n  - Training Centers: Kent, WA; Silverdale, WA.\n\n### 6\\. Scenario (Pressure Question)\n\nThe Safety Lock-Out: \"You see a fellow apprentice working on a panel that hasn't been properly locked out/tagged out because 'the breaker is right there.' What is your immediate response?\"\n\n### 7\\. Grading (Section Total)\n\nInstructor Notes: \\[\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\] Score: \\_\\_\\_\\_ / 30\n\n-----\n\n## TRADE: IRONWORKERS (LOCAL 86)\n\n### 1\\. Pre-Apprentice Questions\n\n  - Describe your experience with heights. Have you ever worked on a deck or roof higher than two stories?\n  - Are you prepared for the physical toll of carrying rebar or connecting steel in all weather conditions?\n\n### 2\\. Ranking Questions\n\n  - How would you rate your physical stamina on a scale of 1-10?\n  - Can you reliably lift and carry 75+ lbs repeatedly throughout a shift?\n\n### 3\\. Union/Local Questions (Local 86)\n\n  - Are you ready to attend the 'Monday Night' apprentice meetings and mandatory school cycles?\n  - What do you know about the \"Boot Camp\" requirements for Ironworker entry?\n\n### 4\\. Non-Union Questions\n\n  - Are you willing to work for a non-union rod-busting crew to get your hours if the hall is slow?\n\n### 5\\. City Options & Locations\n\n  - Training Center: Tukwila, WA.\n\n### 6\\. Scenario (Pressure Question)\n\nThe Open Deck: \"It’s raining, windy, and you’re 40 feet up on open steel. Your partner is moving faster than you and tells you to 'stop being a baby' about the tie-off. How do you respond?\"\n\n### 7\\. Grading (Se...",

      "contentSnippet": "Student Packet: Resume Workshop\n\n# What is the Difference Between a Construction-Facing Resume and a Traditional Resume?\n\n## Construction-Facing Resume\n\n  - Purpose: Designed specifically for getting into a trade, apprenticeship, or construction company.\n  - Focus:\n\n\u003c!-- end list --\u003e\n\n  - Highlights hands-on skills (tools you have used, materials you have worked with).\n  - Includes certifications like OSHA-10, Forklift, Flagger, or CPR.\n  - Shows physical abilities (lifting, standing, operating equipment).\n  - Lists projects or build experiences (tiny houses, ACE stations, shop builds).\n  - Speaks the language of trades (terms like framing, layout, demo, site prep).\n\n\u003c!-- end list --\u003e\n\n  - Experience: Even if you have non-construction jobs, you translate those skills to construction (teamwork, time management, safety awareness).\n\n## Traditional Resume\n\n  - Purpose: Aimed at office, retail, or customer-service jobs.\n  - Focus:\n\n\u003c!-- end list --\u003e\n\n  - Highlights education and past jobs first.\n  - Lists soft skills (communication, organization) but not trade-specific details.\n  - Doesn’t usually include physical skills, certifications, or build projects.\n  - Uses more general wording like “worked with a team” instead of specific trade actions.\n\nKey Takeaway for You:  \nWhen you’re applying for construction, don’t just copy a regular resume. Show them what you can build, operate, or handle on a site. Prove you know safety and can work like an apprentice.\n\n(Optional space for students to write):  \nWrite down three things you will include on your construction-facing resume that you would not bother with on a traditional resume:\n\n-----\n\n-----\n\n# 1\\. Why a Resume Matters in Construction\n\n## Lesson Overview\n\nA resume is your first impression of unions, contractors, and apprenticeships. It shows you are ready to work safely, use tools, and be a dependable team member. We have discussed how it sets you apart even if you are new to construction.\n\n## Instructions\n\nRead the lesson above, then write what you want an employer to know about you in 10 seconds. Be specific and think about how you want to be seen on a job site.\n\nWrite your thoughts:\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_       "contentSnippet": "Handout 1: Transferable Skills for Construction\n\n# Why This Matters\n\nTransferable skills are abilities you’ve developed in other jobs, school, or life experiences that apply directly to construction. These are critical because they show employers that even if you’re new to the industry, you already bring valuable traits to the job site.\n\nAdditional insight: On many job sites, foremen evaluate new hires in the first week based on attitude and adaptability. Showing these skills early can be the difference between being kept on a crew or let go after probation.\n\n# What Are Transferable Skills?\n\n  - Adaptability: Adjusting to new tasks, tools, and environments quickly. (Example: learning a new nail gun model mid-project and completing tasks on time.)\n  - Attention to Detail: Catching mistakes early and ensuring accuracy in all tasks. (Example: spotting a measurement error before cutting expensive materials.)\n  - Leadership: Guiding teammates, delegating tasks, and keeping projects on track. (Example: taking initiative to assign cleanup tasks so a crew could pour concrete without delays.)\n  - Conflict Resolution: Handling disagreements calmly to keep work moving forward. (Example: resolving an argument about material placement by proposing a compromise.)\n  - Work Ethic: Showing reliability, staying focused, and completing tasks without constant supervision. (Example: finishing layout while the lead stepped away.)\n  - Physical Stamina: Maintaining energy and focus through long, active workdays. (Example: working through an intense 10-hour framing day without cutting corners.)\n  - Customer Service: Listening to client needs and solving problems on the spot. (Example: explaining to a homeowner why a schedule changed and earning their trust.)\n  - Technical Learning: Picking up new tools, equipment, or software efficiently. (Example: learning a new digital laser level in a single afternoon.)\n  - Organization: Keeping tools, materials, and paperwork in order for easy access. (Example: staging tools the night before to start faster in the morning.)\n  - Initiative: Stepping up to take on tasks without being asked. (Example: moving extra drywall into the room before the crew ran out.)\n  - Critical Thinking: Evaluating situations and making smart decisions under pressure. (Example: re‑routing an extension cord to prevent a trip hazard.)\n  - Collaboration: Sharing responsibilities and supporting coworkers to reach a common goal. (Example: teaming with another apprentice to finish sheathing ahead of schedule.)\n  - Dependability: Being on time and ready every day, earning trust from your team. (Example: showing up early to prep saws and check measurements.)\n  - Regulatory Compliance: Understanding and following codes, rules, and industry standards. (Example: knowing ladder tie‑off rules and correcting unsafe use.)\n  - Manual Dexterity: Using hands and tools skillfully to complete precise tasks. (Example: hand‑cutting intricate trim angles.)\n  - Problem Anticipation: Spotting potential issues before they become problems. (Example: noticing warped studs and setting them aside before framing.)\n  - Resilience: Staying positive and productive even when work gets tough. (Example: completing tasks during bad weather without complaints.)\n  - Multi‑Tasking: Handling several responsibilities or projects at once. (Example: cutting materials while monitoring a compressor and supporting another task.)\n  - Learning from Feedback: Listening to corrections and applying them immediately. (Example: improving cut quality after one round of feedback.)\n  - Safety Leadership: Encouraging others to follow safety rules and setting the example. (Example: reminding team to wear PPE and modeling safe behavior.)\n\nAdvanced Industry Note: Employers often value apprentices who bring “nontraditional” backgrounds—sports discipline, military training, or caregiving experience all count as transferable skills. Don’t overlook them.\n\n# Real-World Construction Example\n\nA pre‑apprenticeship student joined a volunteer group building tiny homes. She had never been on a job site before, but her teamwork and willingness to ask questions made her stand out. That experience led to a referral for a carpentry apprenticeship.\n\nAdditional example: A former fast‑food worker listed time management and high‑volume workflow as skills; a foreman noted those abilities matched the pace of large commercial projects.\n\n# Write Your Examples Below:\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\n\n\\_\\_...",

      "contentSnippet": "Lesson Plan: Construction Resume Workshop\n\n# Objective:\n\nStudents will create a professional, construction-focused resume that demonstrates transferable skills, job-specific abilities, and readiness for apprenticeship or employment opportunities.\n\n# Standards:\n\n\\- Demonstrates knowledge of resume components and construction-specific terminology.  \n\\- Applies self-reflection to identify transferable and job-specific skills.  \n\\- Utilizes feedback to revise and improve written work.\n\n# Materials Needed:\n\n\\- Resume Workshop slide deck  \n\\- Enhanced handouts packet (Transferable Skills, Construction Skills, Resume Vocabulary, Online Tools)  \n\\- Computers or paper for drafting  \n\\- Printer for final resumes\n\n# Activities:\n\n1\\. Introduction & Discussion (20 min)  \n - Present slides on resume basics and construction-facing differences.  \n - Discuss examples from handouts.  \n2\\. Guided Practice (40 min)  \n - Students complete sections of the handouts with instructor support.  \n - Reflection questions and FAQs used as prompts.  \n3\\. Drafting (30 min)  \n - Students use completed handouts to create a rough draft resume.  \n4\\. Feedback & Revision (30 min)  \n - Instructor returns drafts, discusses common issues, and supports revision.  \n5\\. Finalization (30 min)  \n - Students produce a final version of their resume and print it.\n\n# Assessment:\n\n\\- Formative: Handout completion, class participation, rough draft submission.  \n\\- Summative: Final resume graded with rubric.\n\n# Differentiation:\n\n\\- Provide sentence starters or additional examples for students needing extra support.  \n\\- Offer enrichment tasks (e.g., adding cover letter drafts) for advanced learners.\n\n# Closure:\n\n\\- Students share one skill or accomplishment they are most proud of on their resume.  \n\\- Instructor reinforces the importance of ongoing resume updates.",

      "mimeType": "application/vnd.google-apps.document",
      "fileSize": "74020",
      "parentId": "1Jwu6Ucffb3o-PRepV6hbuOmeQMYT6_tG",
      "contentSnippet": "[Resume Tips Every Trades Professional Should Know](https://russcoinc.com/blog/resume-tips-every-construction-professional-should-know)\n\nHonesty is better than sugarcoated information.\n\n  - This type of resume format highlights actual skills and expertise and includes specific employment dates and history.\n  - Honesty is always the best policy.\n  - Our recommendation would be a combination resume which leads with qualifications and is then followed by employment history.\n  - If you do happen to have many gaps, make sure you drive in hard on your qualifications section. As long as you can speak to any gaps and establish trust with your hiring manager by being honest, you have no reason to worry.\n  - It is common knowledge among hiring managers in the construction field that a lot of projects are short term. therefore, creating a gap in your \"employment history\" which can be frowned upon. Job seekers try and sugarcoat these gaps by using a functional resume format.\n\nStart with the Right Resume Format\n\n  - Gone are the days when a glowing [recommendation](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/sample-letter-of-recommendation) was enough to land your next [construction job](https://www.monster.com/jobs/q-construction-jobs.aspx). Today, construction hiring managers often ask to see a resume, and you could lose a good opportunity if yours isn’t up to speed.\n  - Follow our tips and you will be hammering out a new and improved construction resume in no time:\n  - It’s common for construction jobs to be short-term, so workers may assume that a [functional resume](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/functional-resume-break-tradition) is the best format.\n  - A functional resume is a great way to [job-hustle](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/resume-dilemma-employment-gaps).\n\nUse a [combination resume](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/is-a-combination-resume-right-for-you).\n\n  - This resume format, which leads with a [qualifications summary](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/how-to-write-a-career-summary) and includes a detailed [work history](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/write-a-winning-employment-history), is a better choice for most construction workers.  \n\nObjectives are not commands; they are commitments.\n\n  - Nail a career objective at the very top of your resume. You may be a \"jack of all trades\" but recruiters want to see a precise job target.\n  - Know your audience and cater to the position you are applying for. You can expand on additional skills and specialties in your qualifications section.\n  - If you have more than one objective, create a general resume that can be edited for any construction job you are applying for.\n  - Your objective is to obtain the position, your resume objective should state that loud and clear.\n\nWhy not show off, if you've got something to show.\n\n  - Many positions in the construction industry require specific licenses and certifications, these documents will only strengthen your proven experience.\n  - Be sure to add a section for \"Certifications\" to showcase items like OSHA, MSHA, NCCR and any other training or degrees you may have obtained throughout your work history.\n  - It's also good to include specific job skills in your \"Skills\" section, read over the job description to see what skills are important to the company and tailor your skills to match.\n  - Remember your honesty though, you don't want to be caught lacking in a skill you boasted about on your resume.\n\nThe proof is in the pudding.\n\n  - A lot of construction resumes are very short on the descriptions when it comes to day-to-day responsibilities. Spark your section with providing info on how you actually performed at your job.\n  - Metrics on staying on/under budget, total square footage built within a year, personal accomplishments, are all examples that should be highlighted in your work history.\n  - The devil is in the details, state every fact about the project from foreman to type of facility. Your resume is your marketing tool, don't sell yourself short.\n\n  \nInclude Construction Industry Credentials\n\n  - Add a section for construction industry credentials that employers would find valuable.\n  - List certifications such as OSHA, MSHA and NCCER, and include when and where they were issued.\n\nAlso include your job-specific skills in a [Skills section](https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/resume-skills-section)\n\n  - Review ads for construction jobs to see what skills employers find desirable and incorporate your matching skills into your resume.\n  - Use \u003chttps://www.onetonline.org/\u003e to look up your past jobs and job duties. This website will help you come up with creative ways to explain and show your duties performed in a way that benefits you for the construction industry.\n\n  \nDescribe Your Accomplishments\n\n  - In addition to stating your day-to-day responsibilities, give employers an idea of how well you performed at each construction jo...",

      "contentSnippet": "# Instructor Pathways & Rank‑Up Packet — Seattle Tri‑County\n\nCompiled: 2025-10-20 • Audience: Instructors coaching pre‑apprentices to beat the median applicant (Seattle tri‑county focus).\n\nNorth Star: convert baseline cards into measurable proof of readiness, stack credible credentials, and steer students toward holdover jobs and verifiable practice that moves interview rank and selection odds. Language stays neutral; evidence beats adjectives.\n\n## How to use this packet\n\nGive the student a 90‑day ladder and a proof‑artifact checklist. Evidence matters more than adjectives.\n\nPick a target trade and copy the Rank‑Up Ladder steps. Insert the student’s proof artifacts into the app so the resume/packet reflect real work.\n\nIf a suggestion needs confirmation (e.g., program cadence), mark it “SUGGESTED — NEEDS EVIDENCE” and note the artifact required (email reply, score report, etc.).\n\n## Universal readiness (all trades)\n\nIdentity & contact readiness: government ID, reliable phone/email, City/State shown on resume.\n\nDriver readiness: valid license; if CDL‑oriented trades, begin DOT medical card research and CLP study; maintain a simple driving log (no violations).\n\nAttendance discipline: keep a time‑on‑task log for workshops or practice (dates, hours, supervisor initials).\n\nSafety vocabulary: JHA (Job Hazard Analysis), PPE, LOTO basics; keep a safety checklist you actually used.\n\nMath & prints: ratios, fraction/decimal, unit conversions, tape reading; keep sample sheets with scores and corrections.\n\nCommunication: short 10‑second pitch and one “safety‑under‑pressure” story; write them down and get a coach signature.\n\n## 90‑day Rank‑Up Ladder (copy → paste → customize per student)\n\nWeek 0–2 — quick wins\n\nAutofill resume with measurable bullets (counts, dimensions, tools, prints, torque); remove fluff.\n\nComplete and file baseline cards: Flagger, OSHA‑10, Forklift (classroom card is prep; employer evaluation required).\n\nStart a proof folder (cloud): photos without faces of projects, checklists, signed logs, scores, completion emails.\n\nContact at least 3 holdover employers for the target trade (material handler, prefab/shop helper, maintenance helper); log each contact and reply.\n\nBegin targeted study: vocabulary & nameplates for the trade; upload quiz scores or notes.\n\nWeeks 2–6 — credential + practice\n\nAdd one credential with teeth (trade‑relevant): e.g., EPA 608 for HVAC‑R; EHAP or pesticide Right‑of‑Way study for tree/line; HAZWOPER awareness for laborers where appropriate.\n\nSecure a holdover job or structured volunteer/lab hours; track quantities (feet of material handled, parts counted, prints followed).\n\nMath/print practice (2–3 sessions/week); keep graded sheets or screenshots with dates.\n\nCollect supervisor/coach sign‑offs on safe pace, tool control, and communication under pressure.\n\nWeeks 6–12 — portfolio + applications\n\nAssemble a 1‑page evidence sheet: 6–8 bullets with numbers and a small table of credentials/scores/dates.\n\nRun the application rotation (see Mobility Plan template); screenshot submissions and confirmations.\n\nRequest references based on verified work/logs; attach contact permissions in the packet.\n\n## BFET & direct‑entry on‑ramps (Washington)\n\nIf eligible, use BFET funding to enroll in community‑college entry modules (intro mechanical/electrical/prints/safety). Keep enrollment receipts and completion records.\n\nAsk programs which credit‑bearing courses count for extra points or direct‑entry consideration; store email replies in the proof folder.\n\nAdd college homework artifacts (problem sets, lab sheets) to resume bullets as measured work.\n\n## Mobility Plan — multi‑state application rotation (template)\n\nBuild a 90‑day calendar of application windows (three regions minimum).\n\nCollect relocation readiness items: ID, proof of training, clean copies of cards, driving record, potential housing plan.\n\nTrack each application (date/time, req\\#, contact, response). Export a screenshot/PDF as artifact.\n\nCheck licensing reciprocity (if applicable) before moving; save the governing page or email reply as artifact.\n\n## Holdover jobs that count (generic buckets)\n\nElectrical: material handler, prefab shop assembler, warehouse/runner at electrical contractors.\n\nHVAC‑R/Pipe: parts counter, sheet‑metal shop helper, maintenance helper, shop fabricator trainee.\n\nCivil/Structural: demolition/site cleanup, tool room attendant, concrete laborer trainee.\n\nFacilities: porter/grounds, custodial with documented hazard controls, event setup/stagehand (rigging signals practice).\n\n## Entry tests & physicals — cross‑trade summary\n\nAptitude: algebra/proportions, mechanical reasoning, basic electricity vocabulary; keep practice scores (dated).\n\nPhysicals (as published): timed carry distances, ladder/pole climbs, lift reps; document times/reps with coach initials.\n\nInterview drills: safety scenario, read a print/nameplate, production pace story, tool control, communication under pressure; keep a rubric with coach marks.\n\n# Bo...",
