      "contentSnippet": "Instructor Packet — Stand Out Playbook (Seattle Tri‑County)\n\n# Context\n\nPre‑apprentice grads already hold Flagger, OSHA‑10, and Forklift. This playbook focuses on beyond‑baseline moves that measurably improve selection odds for union and non‑union pathways across King, Pierce, and Snohomish.\n\n# Verify the Basics (what they really mean)\n\nOSHA‑10/30: Outreach cards, not certifications. OSHA Outreach is voluntary awareness training; some employers/owners require it, but it’s not an OSHA “certification.” OSHA‑30 is appropriate for leads/supervisors. \\[Source: OSHA\\]\n\nForklift: Employer must train/evaluate/certify on the specific truck and workplace; evaluation at least every 3 years. Third‑party classes are useful, but the on‑site employer evaluation is still required. \\[Source: OSHA\\]\n\nWA Flagger: Training must meet WAC; expiration ≤ 3 years from issuance and requires photo ID. \\[Source: WA WAC via LII\\]\n\n# Quick Wins by Trade / Target\n\n## Electrical (Inside / Residential / Limited Energy)\n\nProgram reality check (union): PSEJATC Inside Wire ≈ 8,000 OJT + \\~1,000 classroom hours leading to WA (01) Journeyman after the state exam. Tri‑county work jurisdiction applies. Coach math readiness and expectations. \\[Source: PSEJATC\\]\n\nDocumented tool time: conduit measuring, layout, pulls, terminations (even under supervision).\n\nLow‑voltage crossover: labeling, testing, as‑built updates.\n\nHoldover jobs: material handler, prefab shop, warehouse/runner at electrical contractors.\n\nFree/cheap study: code vocabulary, print reading, and safe energy‑control habits; capture as resume bullets (measured work, verified torque).\n\n## HVAC/R & Pipe Trades (Plumber / Steamfitter / HVAC‑R)\n\nUnion anchor: Seattle Area Pipe Trades (UA Local 32) — multiple programs (HVAC‑R, Steamfitter, Plumber). Use official pages for expectations and contacts. \\[Source: UA Local 32\\]\n\nCertification with teeth: EPA Section 608 — Type I/II/III or Universal (does not expire). Add type explicitly on resume. \\[Source: EPA\\]\n\nHoldover jobs: parts counter, shop assistant, sheet‑metal fab helper, maintenance tech trainee.\n\n## Outside Power (Lineman) & Power Line Clearance Tree Trimmer\n\nTree Trimmer (NW Line JATC): Applications accepted year‑round; due by 12pm the first Monday for that month’s ranking. Extra points exist (ISA, Pesticide Laws & Safety, Right‑of‑Way, CDL, degrees, military, etc.). Include full details page. \\[Source: NW Line JATC\\]\n\nContact hub: administrative office phone/email/hours/address for NW Line JATC (ask about current openings and CDL expectations). \\[Source: NW Line JATC\\]\n\nBridge programs: VOLTA Line School — feeder into outside line/tree work. \\[Source: NW Line JATC\\]\n\nStand‑out stack: CDL‑B/A, ISA coursework, flagger, First Aid/CPR, pesticide categories (Right‑of‑Way), documented rigging/ground ops, storm‑response readiness.\n\n# Cross‑Trade Beyond‑Baseline Moves\n\nLevel up OSHA: For candidates trending toward lead roles, OSHA‑30 adds credibility (cite correctly as “OSHA Outreach 30‑Hour – Construction”). \\[Source: OSHA\\]\n\nForklift leverage: With a classroom card, coach students to request on‑truck employer certification early; keep the evaluation record (name, date, evaluator, truck). \\[Source: OSHA\\]\n\nEPA 608 (HVAC/R‑adjacent): One weekend of study + proctored test → durable credential. \\[Source: EPA\\]\n\nVeterans pipeline: Helmets to Hardhats connects directly to JATCs and building trades. \\[Source: Helmets to Hardhats\\]\n\n# Local Anchors to Include (Tri‑County)\n\nElectrical (PSEJATC): Inside/Limited Energy/Residential pages — program hours, algebra requirement, campus info (Renton + satellite). \\[Source: PSEJATC\\]\n\nPipe Trades (UA Local 32): Program overview and contacts. \\[Source: UA Local 32\\]\n\nIronworkers Local 86 (North Seattle College): Apprenticeship overview, wage progression, contact — useful even for non‑union prospects. \\[Source: North Seattle College\\]\n\nOutside Power/Tree Trimmer (NW Line JATC): Application rhythm, points, benefits, contact. \\[Source: NW Line JATC\\]\n\n# Resume & Holdover Job Tactics\n\nConvert baseline cards into concrete bullets (evidence beats adjectives). Examples:\n\n“Completed OSHA Outreach 10‑Hour (Construction); applied JHA/LOTO vocabulary on shop projects.”\n\n“Forklift: employer‑certified on sit‑down electric in warehouse—evaluation current.”\n\nHoldover jobs that count:\n\nMaterial handler at electrical or mechanical contractors; prefab shop helper; tool room/parts counter.\n\nFacilities maintenance helper; demolition/site cleanup (document PPE and hazard controls).\n\nTraffic control with leadership shifts (document radios, lane setups, and close‑out checklists).\n\nEvidence \\\u003e adjectives: log quantities, measurements, prints followed, tools used, and who verified (lead/foreman). Turn that into resume bullets and interview stories.\n\n# What the App Must Do (Integration Requirements)\n\nKeep this “Stand Out” section in the Instructor Pathway Packet after workshop reflections and before full‑text attachments.\n\nPreserve ...",

  "fileContent": "# Applying for Hold Over Jobs  \n\n# **Applying for “Hold-Over” Jobs While You Wait for Apprenticeship**\n\n## **1. Why this matters**\n\nIn Washington, there are thousands of active construction apprentices and more entering every year. Many of them are women and people of color entering through programs like ANEW and other pre-apprenticeships.[tradeswomenbuild.org](https://tradeswomenbuild.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/06/anew-paper-how-policy-and-collaboration-is-changing-the-face-of-construction-in-seattle-1.pdf)\n\nBut:\n\n  - Apprenticeship entry is competitive.  \n      \n  - Most programs rank applicants and only pull from the top as work becomes available.  \n      \n  - It can take months between interviews or “pulls” from the list.  \n      \n  - The construction job market goes up and down. In the last year, Washington actually lost over 11,000 construction jobs, even though employers still report they need skilled workers.[KIRO 7 News Seattle  \n      \n    ](https://www.kiro7.com/news/local/washington-construction-jobs-fall-short-amid-nationwide-growth/MUBBU244WZBOBLNNCRZVNJPF34/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou cannot control when you get called from an apprenticeship list.\n\nYou can control what you do in between.\n\nA “hold-over job” is a job you work while you are waiting for apprenticeship:\n\n  - It pays your bills.  \n      \n  - It keeps you around tools, sites, and industry people.  \n      \n  - It can build hours and experience that may help you later, if you do it correctly and legally.  \n      \n\nThis lesson shows you how to:\n\n1.  Find hold-over jobs.  \n      \n2.  Check if the employer is legal and safe.  \n      \n3.  Understand electrical and plumbing trainee cards.  \n      \n4.  Avoid fake “apprenticeships.”  \n      \n5.  Use public training programs like BEAM or King County’s Operator-in-Training.  \n      \n6.  Protect your hours, your body, and your rights.  \n      \n\n## **2. Key terms (plain language)**\n\n  - **Hold-over job** – A job you do in construction or a related field while you wait to enter your chosen apprenticeship.  \n      \n  - **Open shop / non-union** – A contractor that is not signatory to a union. They can still be legal and legit, or they can be a complete mess. You have to check.  \n      \n  - **Registered apprenticeship** – An apprenticeship program approved by the Washington State Apprenticeship and Training Council (through L\\&I) or the U.S. Department of Labor. This is what leads to a recognized journey card.[Apprenticeship.gov+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.apprenticeship.gov/employers/registered-apprenticeship-program?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - **Training agent** – An employer approved to employ apprentices in a specific registered program. They show up under that program in the state’s apprenticeship system.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/apprenticeship-registration-and-tracking-system?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - **Trainee card (electrical / plumbing)** – A license from L\\&I that allows you to legally work as an electrical or plumbing trainee under supervision and log hours toward future licensing.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n  - **Journey-level worker** – Someone who has completed a registered apprenticeship or met the legal experience requirements and passed the state exam.[tradeswomenbuild.org+1  \n      \n    ](https://tradeswomenbuild.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/06/anew-paper-how-policy-and-collaboration-is-changing-the-face-of-construction-in-seattle-1.pdf)\n\n## \n\n## **3. Big picture: What a “good” hold-over job does for you**\n\nA good hold-over job should:\n\n1.  Keep you close to your target trade (or at least the construction industry).  \n      \n2.  Pay at or above legal minimum wage.  \n      \n      \n      - Washington state minimum wage in 2025 is $16.66/hour; some local cities (Seattle, Renton, Tukwila, SeaTac, unincorporated King County) have higher minimum wages over $20/hour.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n          \n        ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/wages/minimum-wage/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n3.  Follow basic worker rights (rest breaks, overtime after 40 hours/week, workers’ comp coverage).[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/workplace-policies/rest-breaks-meal-periods-and-schedules?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n4.  Not require you to break the law (for example, doing electrical work without a trainee card).  \n      \n5.  Ideally, build usable experience and certifications (hours, OSHA-10, forklift, flagger, etc.).  \n      \n\nA bad hold-over job:\n\n  - Pays below legal minimum.  \n      \n  - Pushes you to work as a “1099” contractor just to dodge taxes and workers’ comp.  \n      \n  - Skips rest breaks, overtime pay, or safety gear.  \n      \n  - Calls you an “apprentice” but is not a registered apprenticeship.  \n      \n  - Has no L\\&I contractor registration or a history of serious violations.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business)\n\nYour goal is not “any job.” Your goal is a legal, safe job that helps your long-term plan.\n\n## **4. Step-by-step workflow for finding hold-over jobs**\n\n### **Step 1: Choose your lane for this season**\n\nYou do not need your forever job. You need your next six to twelve months.\n\nClarify:\n\n1.  Which trades are you targeting long-term? (Example: inside electrician, carpenter, laborer, operator, plumber, lineworker.)  \n      \n2.  What can you realistically handle right now?  \n      \n      \n      - Commute.  \n          \n      - Hours (swing, nights, weekends).  \n          \n      - Childcare and family responsibilities.  \n          \n3.  How close to the tools do you want to be?  \n      \n      \n      - Option A: Direct trade-adjacent work (laborer, installer, shop helper, traffic control, material handler).  \n          \n      - Option B: Industry-support work (warehouse, tool yard, prefab shop, utility trainee programs).  \n          \n\nWrite that down. This guides your search keywords and decisions.\n\n  \n\n### **Step 2: Build your online job-search tools**\n\nYou are going to see the same companies across multiple sites. That is fine. You want visibility.\n\nAt a minimum, set up:\n\n1.  **Indeed** – For construction labor, helpers, installers, “apprentice” titles in open-shop companies.  \n      \n2.  **Glassdoor** – To read employee reviews and basic pay info before you apply.  \n      \n3.  **(Optional but smart) State or local job boards****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - GovernmentJobs.com for public sector jobs like King County or City of Seattle.  \n          \n      - Local utility and public-agency career pages (King County, Seattle City Light, Sound Transit, WSDOT, Port of Seattle, etc.).  \n          \n\nBasic profile setup:\n\n  - Use a simple, professional email.  \n      \n  - Put your current pre-apprenticeship and certifications at the top:  \n      \n      \n      - Example: “ANEW Pre-Apprenticeship Graduate – Construction Basics, OSHA-10, Forklift (if completed).”  \n          \n  - Keep location accurate; most employers filter by distance.  \n      \n\nSearch keywords to try:\n\n  - “\\[Your trade\\] helper” (ex: “electrical helper,” “plumbing helper,” “concrete laborer”).  \n      \n  - “Construction laborer.”  \n      \n  - “Installer” (solar, low-voltage, HVAC, fire sprinkler, insulation, windows, doors).  \n      \n  - “Operator-in-training,” “pre-apprentice,” “trainee,” “utility worker.”  \n      \n\nSave searches and turn on alerts. Let the sites work for you every day.\n\n## **5. How to check a contractor with L\\&I (non-negotiable)**\n\nBefore you get excited about a hold-over job, verify the employer.\n\n### **5.1 Verify they are properly registered**\n\nWashington L\\&I has a public “Verify a Contractor, Tradesperson, or Business” tool.[Washington Labor & Industries](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business)\n\nUse it every time:\n\n1.  Go to L\\&I’s verification page.  \n      \n2.  Search by:  \n      \n      \n      - Contractor’s business name,  \n          \n      - UBI number (if listed), or  \n          \n      - License number (if listed).  \n          \n3.  Check these items:  \n      \n      \n      - “Status” – must be “Active.”  \n          \n      - Bond and insurance – must be current.  \n          \n      - Any recent infractions, unpaid debts, or license suspensions.  \n          \n\nIf they are not in the system or their status is suspended, that is a serious red flag.\n\n### **5.2 Check if they are a training agent or connected to a registered apprenticeship**\n\nFor work you hope will turn into recognized apprenticeship experience, check whether the program and employer are in the state apprenticeship system.\n\nWashington’s L\\&I “Become an apprentice” pages explain that only apprentices in registered programs get the full benefits of apprenticeship, including recognized journey-level status.[Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/become-an-apprentice?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou can:\n\n1.  Use the L\\&I Apprenticeship Program search.  \n      \n2.  Look up:  \n      \n      \n      - The program name (for example, “Puget Sound Electrical JATC”).  \n          \n      - The occupation (for example, “Electrician – Inside Wireman”).  \n          \n      - The county.  \n          \n3.  Open the program and look for “training agents/employers.”  \n      \n\nIf the employer says they have “apprentices,” but:\n\n  - They do not show up in the state system,  \n      \n  - They cannot tell you the name of the program sponsor,  \n      \n  - Or they get defensive when you ask,  \n      \n\nthen you are not in a registered apprenticeship. You are just an employee being called an “apprentice.”\n\nThat does not automatically mean “never take the job,” but you need to know that those hours may not count toward a journey card.\n\n## \n\n## **6. Electrical trainee card (Washington State)**\n\nElectrical work is heavily regulated in Washington. You cannot legally perform electrical work on a job site without the right license or trainee status.\n\nWashington L\\&I is extremely clear:\n\n  - You must have a valid electrical trainee certificate to work as an electrical trainee.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n  - You must work for a properly licensed electrical contractor.  \n      \n  - Your work must be supervised by a certified electrician and within legal supervision ratios.  \n      \n  - Experience hours only count if you follow all of those rules and your employer submits proper affidavits of experience to L\\&I.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n\n### **6.1 Basic requirements (at a high level)**\n\nFrom L\\&I’s electrical trainee guidance:[Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n\n  - Minimum age: 16.  \n      \n  - You must apply for and receive an electrical trainee certificate from L\\&I before doing electrical work.  \n      \n  - Your trainee card is valid for a specific period (usually 2 years) and must be renewed.  \n      \n  - You must complete at least 48 hours of approved basic classroom instruction every 2-year renewal cycle to renew the card.[Washington Labor & Industries  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business)\n  - You must work under supervision of a certified electrician and within allowed ratios (this varies by specialty).  \n      \n\nIf you work without:\n\n  - An active trainee card,  \n      \n  - A licensed contractor,  \n      \n  - Proper supervision,  \n      \n\nL\\&I may treat those hours as illegal and they will not count toward exam or licensing requirements.[Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n\n### **6.2 What this means for you in a hold-over job**\n\nIf you want electrical:\n\n  - If a non-union contractor offers you electrical work:  \n      \n      \n      - Step 1: Confirm they are a licensed electrical contractor on the L\\&I verification site.[Washington Labor & Industries  \n          \n        ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business)\n      - Step 2: Apply for your electrical trainee certificate before doing electrical work.  \n          \n      - Step 3: Confirm they are willing to:  \n          \n          \n          - Verify your trainee card,  \n              \n          - Supervise you properly,  \n              \n          - Submit affidavits of experience to L\\&I.  \n              \n\nQuestions to ask the employer:\n\n1.  “Are you a licensed electrical contractor with L\\&I?”  \n      \n2.  “Will I be hired as a registered electrical trainee with an L\\&I trainee certificate?”  \n      \n3.  “Do you submit affidavits of experience for your trainees so their hours count with L\\&I?”  \n      \n\nIf they cannot answer these clearly or they tell you “we don’t worry about that here,” you are being asked to break the law and throw away your hours.\n\n## \n\n## **7. Plumbing trainee card (Washington State)**\n\nPlumbing has a similar system.\n\nWashington L\\&I’s plumber trainee guidance says:[Washington Labor & Industries+2ServiceTitan+2](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/plumbing/plumber-certification/plumber-trainee)\n\n  - You must have a plumber trainee certificate to legally gain experience towards becoming a certified plumber.  \n      \n  - You must work under the supervision of a certified journey-level or residential plumber.  \n      \n  - All experience hours must be for a registered contractor under proper supervision.  \n      \n  - Hours earned when you did not hold a valid trainee certificate will not be credited toward plumber certification.  \n      \n\nThere are also continuing education requirements for plumbers, and plumbers must pass exams that test both knowledge and code.\n\n### **7.1 What this means for a plumbing hold-over job**\n\nIf you want plumbing, and a non-union shop offers you plumbing work:\n\n  - Confirm they are a licensed plumbing contractor in L\\&I’s system.[Washington Labor & Industries  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business)\n  - Apply for your plumber trainee card before you start doing plumbing tasks.  \n      \n  - Confirm that:  \n      \n      \n      - Your supervisor is a certified plumber.  \n          \n      - The employer submits experience records according to L\\&I rules.  \n          \n\nAgain, “plumber’s helper” without a trainee card may feel like experience, but it may not count legally toward a license.\n\n## **8. How to protect your hours (electrical, plumbing, or other)**\n\nEven if your immediate goal is “I need a paycheck,” think long-term. For regulated trades (electrical, plumbing) your licensing will depend on hours that L\\&I actually recognizes.[Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/electrical/electrical-licensing-exams-education/electrical-trainee)\n\n### **8.1 Personal hours log**\n\nKeep your own record, in addition to whatever the employer files. At minimum, track:\n\n  - Employer name  \n      \n  - Job site / project  \n      \n  - Dates worked  \n      \n  - Type of work (rough description)  \n      \n  - Hours per day  \n      \n  - Supervisor’s name  \n      \n\nExample structure:\n\n|  |  |  |  |  |  |\n| :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: | :-: |\n| \\*\\*Month\\*\\* | \\*\\*Employer\\*\\* | \\*\\*Site\\*\\* | \\*\\*Trade / tasks\\*\\* | \\*\\*Total hours\\*\\* | \\*\\*Supervisor\\*\\* |\n\nKeep copies of:\n\n  - Pay stubs  \n      \n  - Timesheets  \n      \n  - Any “affidavits of experience” or documentation submitted to L\\&I  \n      \n\nIf you ever switch employers, you will need this paper trail.\n\n### **8.2 Confirm what will and will not transfer**\n\nImportant reality:\n\n  - L\\&I decides whether hours count for licensing and exams.  \n      \n  - Individual apprenticeship programs and unions decide how many “outside” hours they are willing to accept toward their program completion.  \n      \n\nYou should:\n\n1.  Treat all legit hours as useful.  \n      \n2.  Assume that not all non-union hours will automatically shorten your apprenticeship.  \n      \n3.  Ask the specific apprenticeship program later how they handle prior experience.  \n      \n\nYour hold-over job is mainly about staying in the game, building real experience, and avoiding illegal or exploitative situations.\n\n## \n\n## **9. “In-house apprenticeship” vs registered apprenticeship**\n\nYou will see postings that say things like:\n\n  - “We have our own apprenticeship.”  \n      \n  - “Company apprenticeship program – no union required.”  \n      \n  - “Learn as you go, we’ll apprentice you.”  \n      \n\nWashington L\\&I warns:\n\nIf a company hires you informally as an “apprentice,” and the apprenticeship is not officially registered with the state or federal government, you will not receive the benefits of a registered apprenticeship, including working as a journey-level professional.[ Washington Labor & Industries](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/become-an-apprentice?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nThe U.S. Department of Labor likewise defines **registered apprenticeship** as a program that leads to a nationally recognized credential, with structured on-the-job learning and related instruction.[Apprenticeship.gov+1](https://www.apprenticeship.gov/employers/registered-apprenticeship-program?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n### **9.1 How to check if it’s real**\n\nAsk the employer:\n\n1.  “Is this a Washington-registered apprenticeship program?”  \n      \n2.  “What is the official name of the apprenticeship sponsor?”  \n      \n3.  “Are you listed as a training agent with that program?”  \n      \n\nThen:\n\n1.  Use the L\\&I apprenticeship program search to look up that program.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/apprenticeship-registration-and-tracking-system?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n2.  Confirm:  \n      \n      \n      - The program exists.  \n          \n      - The occupation matches what they told you.  \n          \n      - The employer is actually listed as a training agent.  \n          \n\nIf the answer is “no,” then you are in some kind of internal training program, not a registered apprenticeship.\n\nThat is not automatically bad as a hold-over job. It is just different:\n\n  - It can give you experience, references, and maybe certifications.  \n      \n  - It does not give you a recognized journey card by itself.  \n      \n  - You may still need to enter a registered apprenticeship later and complete it.  \n      \n\nGo in with your eyes open.\n\n## \n\n## **10. Using public-sector training programs as hold-over options**\n\nNot all hold-over jobs are with private contractors. Some of the best “bridge” jobs are public training programs that pay you to learn and often feed into long-term, union careers.\n\n### **10.1 King County Wastewater Treatment – Operator-in-Training (OIT)**\n\nKing County’s Wastewater Treatment Division (WTD) runs an **Operator-in-Training Program**:\n\n  - It is a six-month, paid on-the-job training program in wastewater operations.  \n      \n  - 2024 starting wages are around $27.36/hour for utility worker/OIT positions, with step increases as you progress.[King County  \n      \n    ](https://kingcounty.gov/en/dept/dnrp/waste-services/wastewater-treatment/about/join-our-team/operator-in-training?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - During the program, you are required to pass the Washington Department of Ecology Wastewater Operator-in-Training certification exam within about six months.[King County+1  \n      \n    ](https://kingcounty.gov/en/dept/dnrp/waste-services/wastewater-treatment/about/join-our-team/operator-in-training?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - The program has been recognized nationally and has filled more than 70 operator positions while increasing racial and gender diversity in the workforce.[King County  \n      \n    ](https://kingcounty.gov/en/dept/dnrp/about-king-county/about-dnrp/newsroom/2024-news-releases/02-22-operator-in-training?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nFor a pre-apprentice:\n\n  - This is not a building-trades apprenticeship, but it is a union public-sector operations job.  \n      \n  - It pays well, has benefits, and is a real career path in its own right.  \n      \n  - It is an excellent hold-over or long-term option if you like heavy industrial work, systems, and public service.  \n      \n\n### **10.2 Seattle City Light – BEAM (Basic Electricity and Applied Math)**\n\nBEAM is a course designed and run by Seattle City Light in partnership with South Seattle College:\n\n  - It is a non-credit class and lab that covers basic electrical theory and trades math.[seattlecolleges.edu+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.seattlecolleges.edu/sites/seattlecolleges.southseattle.edu/files/2024-05/Seattle%20City%20Light%203997.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - BEAM is recognized as a pre-apprenticeship-style program that prepares students for electrical careers and can satisfy entry requirements for certain City of Seattle apprenticeships.[georgetown.southseattle.edu+1  \n      \n    ](https://georgetown.southseattle.edu/apprenticeship-pre-apprenticeships/faqs?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nFor you:\n\n  - If you are aiming for electrical or linework, BEAM is a strong way to stay in the game between apprenticeship application cycles.  \n      \n  - It deepens your math and theory and gives you something powerful to add to your resume.  \n      \n\n### **10.3 Seattle City Light – Pre-Apprentice Lineworker (PAL)**\n\nSeattle City Light also runs a **Pre-Apprentice Lineworker (PAL)** program:\n\n  - It is a six-month paid training position.  \n      \n  - PALs work outdoors with experienced lineworkers learning field basics and preparing for the Lineworker Apprenticeship.[GovernmentJobs  \n      \n    ](https://www.governmentjobs.com/careers/seattle/jobs/newprint/5039672?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nFor you:\n\n  - PAL is both a hold-over job and a direct on-ramp to a high-wage, high-risk, high-skill trade.  \n      \n  - Entry is competitive, but it is worth tracking if you are interested in linework.  \n      \n\n### **10.4 Other examples**\n\nThere are many similar programs:\n\n  - Workforce development cohorts and internship programs at King County Wastewater.[King County  \n      \n    ](https://kingcounty.gov/en/dept/dnrp/waste-services/wastewater-treatment/about/join-our-team/workforce-development?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - Apprenticeship preparation programs listed by L\\&I and local colleges.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/apprenticeship-preparation?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYour job:\n\n  - Regularly search for “operator-in-training,” “pre-apprentice,” “trainee,” and “utility worker” on GovernmentJobs.com, county and city job pages, and local utilities.  \n      \n\n## **11. Resume and profile strategy for hold-over jobs**\n\nYour resume for hold-over jobs does not have to be fancy. It does have to be clear and honest.\n\n### **11.1 What to highlight**\n\nTop of resume:\n\n  - Pre-apprenticeship and training  \n      \n      \n      - Example: “ANEW Pre-Apprenticeship Graduate – 280 hours of construction basics, safety, and hands-on skills.”  \n          \n  - Certifications:  \n      \n      \n      - OSHA-10 Construction  \n          \n      - Forklift, flagger, first aid/CPR, etc.  \n          \n  - Any relevant past work:  \n      \n      \n      - Warehouse, maintenance, janitorial, fast food, retail, security, caregiving.  \n          \n\nTranslate your experience into construction language:\n\n  - “Showed up on time every day for early morning shifts.”  \n      \n  - “Worked safely around customers and co-workers.”  \n      \n  - “Followed written procedures and checklists.”  \n      \n  - “Used hand tools and basic power tools.”  \n      \n\nThese are exactly what contractors want in entry-level hires.\n\n### **11.2 What to say about apprenticeship**\n\nDo not hide that you are applying for apprenticeship. Frame it correctly:\n\n  - “Currently applying to registered apprenticeship programs for \\[trade\\]. Seeking hold-over work to continue building skills and experience in the industry.”  \n      \n\nEmployers who are serious will respect the honesty. Some will like that you are hungry to learn.\n\n## \n\n## **12. Red flags and your rights in non-union jobs**\n\nYou might decide to work open-shop while you wait. That is a valid choice if you protect yourself.\n\nKnow your minimum rights:\n\n  - In 2025, Washington’s minimum wage is $16.66/hour statewide and higher in some cities (for example, Seattle $20.76, Tukwila $21.10 for many large employers).[Human Resource Services+3Washington Labor & Industries+3Washington Labor & Industries+3  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/wages/minimum-wage/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - Most workers must be paid overtime (1.5x) for hours over 40 in a week.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/wages/overtime/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - You must receive rest breaks and meal periods under state law, although construction CBAs can adjust how these work.[Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/workplace-policies/rest-breaks-meal-periods-and-schedules?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - Wage theft (being underpaid, not paid, or denied overtime/breaks) is illegal.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Emery Reddy+2  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/forms-publications/F101-165-909.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nMajor red flags:\n\n  - “You’ll be a 1099, just sign this and you’re responsible for your own taxes and workers’ comp.”  \n      \n  - “We can’t put you on payroll yet, but come work and we’ll pay you cash.”  \n      \n  - “We don’t really do breaks here.”  \n      \n  - “We call you an apprentice, but there is no paperwork with L\\&I.”  \n      \n  - “Bring all your own PPE and we won’t reimburse you.”  \n      \n\nConstruction workers are commonly misclassified as independent contractors so employers can dodge taxes, minimum wage, and workers’ comp.[Washington Labor & Industries+2Sharpe Law Firm PLLC+2](https://www.lni.wa.gov/insurance/insurance-requirements/independent-contractors/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou always have the right to:\n\n  - Ask for your pay stub and payroll details.  \n      \n  - Ask which wage law applies (state or local).  \n      \n  - Contact L\\&I’s Employment Standards Program if you think something is wrong.[masterbuilderspierce.com+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n      \n    ](https://masterbuilderspierce.com/washingtons-2025-minimum-wage-increase/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n## \n\n## **13. Putting it all together – student checklist**\n\nUse this as your personal checklist for hold-over jobs.\n\n1.  Clarify your target trade and your limits (commute, childcare, schedule).  \n      \n2.  Set up or update:  \n      \n      \n      - Indeed  \n          \n      - Glassdoor  \n          \n      - Local/government job profiles (King County, City of Seattle, etc.).  \n          \n3.  Search daily/weekly with targeted keywords.  \n      \n4.  For each job you’re interested in:  \n      \n      \n      - Look up the employer in L\\&I’s “Verify a Contractor or Tradesperson” tool.  \n          \n      - Confirm they are registered and active.  \n          \n5.  If the work is electrical:  \n      \n      \n      - Get or renew your electrical trainee card.  \n          \n      - Confirm the contractor is a licensed electrical contractor.  \n          \n      - Confirm they will supervise you properly and submit affidavits.  \n          \n6.  If the work is plumbing:  \n      \n      \n      - Get or renew your plumber trainee card.  \n          \n      - Confirm you will work under a certified plumber and the employer will submit hours.  \n          \n7.  If they claim “apprenticeship”:  \n      \n      \n      - Ask which registered apprenticeship program.  \n          \n      - Look it up in L\\&I’s apprenticeship program list.  \n          \n      - Decide if this is a real apprenticeship, a strong training job, or just a label.  \n          \n8.  Apply to at least one public-sector training or pre-apprentice-style program (OIT, BEAM, PAL, workforce development cohorts) if it fits your goals.  \n      \n9.  Keep your own hours log and copies of pay stubs.  \n      \n10. Monitor your pay, breaks, and safety. If something is off, talk to your instructor, a trusted mentor, or L\\&I.  \n      \n\nYou are allowed to take a hold-over job that is not perfect. The goal is not perfection; the goal is progress without getting exploited or throwing away your future license.\n\nIf you follow this process, your “in-between” time becomes part of your career, not a detour.\n\n  \n  \n\n# Contractor - L$I FAQ  \n\n## **5. How to Check a Contractor with L\\&I – Deep FAQ (Washington State)**\n\n**Read this before you say yes to any “apprentice” or “trainee” job.****  \n** You’re in Washington. That means **L\\&I (Department of Labor & Industries)** controls:\n\n  - Contractor registration and bonding  \n      \n  - Workers’ comp coverage  \n      \n  - Electrical and plumbing licensing  \n      \n  - Registered apprenticeship rules  \n      \n\nIf the contractor isn’t lined up with L\\&I, your hours can disappear on paper even if your body did the work.[ Washington Labor & Industries](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/register-as-a-contractor/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n### **Q1. What’s the bare minimum a contractor must have before they can legally hire me?**\n\nIn Washington, a construction contractor must:\n\n1.  **Be registered with L\\&I as a contractor** (or licensed as an electrical or plumbing contractor if they do that work).  \n      \n2.  Have a **bond and general liability insurance** on file with L\\&I, under the correct legal business name.  \n      \n3.  Have an **active workers’ compensation account** and be reporting/pay\u00ading premiums for employees.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/register-as-a-contractor/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou check this using **L\\&I’s “Verify a Contractor, Tradesperson or Business” tool.** L\\&I says this lets you see if a contractor is properly registered, bonded, insured, and covered by workers’ comp.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n**Student checklist (minimum legal):**\n\n  - Status = **Active**, not suspended or expired  \n      \n  - **Bond** and **insurance** listed as current  \n      \n  - **Workers’ comp** account = active / in good standing, not “closed” or “decertified”  \n      \n\nIf any of those are missing or dead, that is a **hard no**.\n\n### **Q2. How do I use L\\&I’s verify tool and actually read what I’m looking at?**\n\n**Step 1 – Search them.****  \n** Use L\\&I’s verify page. Search by **business name** or **license number**. If there are multiple similar names, match the **city** and any DBA (“doing business as”) you see on their website or paperwork.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n**Step 2 – Check these items on the page:**\n\n  - **Contractor registration status:** must say **Active**.  \n      \n  - **Bond & insurance:** should show policy info and that it’s current.  \n      \n  - **Workers’ comp account:** shows whether they’re **current or delinquent**.  \n      \n  - **Enforcement / violations section:** scroll down. L\\&I’s page shows safety violations, infractions, or lawsuits against the bond where they had to pay out for unpaid wages or other problems.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n**Red flags:**\n\n  - Registration suspended or expired more than once  \n      \n  - Repeated workers’ comp problems  \n      \n  - Bond lawsuits or multiple serious safety violations close together  \n      \n\nNone of this means “never work there.” It does mean: **go in with eyes open and ask questions.**\n\n### **Q3. Who is actually allowed to “train” me as an apprentice?**\n\nThere are two different systems you care about:\n\n1.  **Registered apprenticeship (carpenters, laborers, operating engineers, etc.)****  \n      \n    **\n2.  **License-based trainee systems (electrical and plumbing)****  \n      \n    **\n\n#### **3A. Registered apprenticeship (carpenter, laborer, etc.)**\n\nFor apprenticeship hours to count in Washington, all three things must be true:\n\n  - You are a **registered apprentice** in a WSATC-approved program.  \n      \n  - The company is an **approved Training Agent** under that specific program.[ Washington State Legislature  \n      \n    ](https://app.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=296-05-003&utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - The work you’re doing matches the **work processes** in that program’s standards.  \n      \n\nProgram standards and WAC rules say that sponsors must only allow employers to train apprentices if they can provide proper on-the-job training and supervision, and those employers sign **training agent agreements** promising to follow the standards.[ Washington Labor & Industries](https://www.lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/apprenticeship/_docs/0095.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nIf the employer is **not** a training agent for that program, then legally you’re just a regular employee. You can still learn skills, but **those hours do not automatically count** toward that apprenticeship term unless the sponsor later chooses to grant you credit after reviewing your experience.\n\n#### **3B. Electrical and plumbing trainees**\n\nFor **electrical trainees**:\n\n  - You must have an active **electrical trainee card**.  \n      \n  - You must work for a **licensed electrical contractor** with a properly licensed administrator/electrician.  \n      \n  - Your hours must meet L\\&I’s supervision and work rules in RCW 19.28 and WAC 296-46B (wrong supervision or wrong type of work = hours rejected).  \n      \n\nFor **plumber trainees**:\n\n  - You must have an active **plumber trainee certificate**.  \n      \n  - Work must be under a **certified plumber** and a registered plumbing contractor.  \n      \n  - Supervision ratios (often one journeyman to one trainee for commercial work) have to be followed or hours can be denied.  \n      \n\nIf any of that is missing—no license, no supervision, expired card—**L\\&I can and does refuse to count your hours.**[ Washington Labor & Industries](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/plumbing/plumber-certification/plumber-trainee?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n### **Q4. Are contractors required to report my hours, or is it all on me?**\n\nIt depends which system you’re in. The reality is: **if you don’t manage it, you’re the one who loses.**\n\n#### **4A. Electrical trainees**\n\n  - Every **2 years** when your trainee card expires, it is **your responsibility** to report your hours to L\\&I.  \n      \n  - To do that, you must request **Affidavits of Experience** from each employer; L\\&I says employers have **20 days** to give them back to you.  \n      \n  - L\\&I will only accept hours that were **legally obtained** (licensed contractor, proper supervision, permits etc.).  \n      \n\nSo: the employer is required to truthfully sign and notarize what you did, but **you are the one who has to chase the paperwork and submit the original forms**.\n\n#### **4B. Plumber trainees**\n\n  - Plumber trainees must send L\\&I **notarized affidavits of experience** for each employer/supervisor.  \n      \n  - Affidavits are due **no later than 30 days after your renewal date**.  \n      \n  - L\\&I explicitly says you **may not receive credit** for hours if your card wasn’t active, supervision ratios weren’t followed, or affidavits are incomplete/late.[ Washington Labor & Industries  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/plumbing/plumber-certification/plumber-trainee?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nAgain: the employer/supervisor signs under oath, but **you** must make sure those forms get in on time.\n\n#### **4C. Registered apprenticeship (carpenter, laborer, operating engineer, etc.)**\n\n  - State apprenticeship rules say sponsors must keep complete records of each apprentice’s hours and training and report to L\\&I.  \n      \n  - Program standards almost always say **you must turn in work-process hours monthly**. Example: the Northwest Laborers program requires working apprentices to submit hours weekly and says hours not reported by the 7th of the following month **will not count** toward your term.  \n      \n\nSo in apprenticeship, there’s a three-way chain:\n\n1.  **You** submit timesheets/online logs by the deadline.  \n      \n2.  The **training agent** confirms the hours.  \n      \n3.  The **sponsor** enters them into ARTS / program records and reports to L\\&I.  \n      \n\nMiss a step, you lose time.\n\n### **Q5. If I work for a non-union contractor that isn’t a training agent, will my hours count?**\n\nPlain answer: **usually no.**\n\n  - L\\&I only treats hours in a **registered program** as apprenticeship hours.  \n      \n  - Some programs may give “advanced standing” later for previous experience, but that’s **completely up to the sponsor** and not guaranteed.  \n      \n\nOn public works jobs, there’s another twist:\n\n  - If you are not a registered apprentice, the contractor must pay you at the **full journey-level prevailing wage** for that trade; they cannot legally pay you an “apprentice” rate.[ MRSC  \n      \n    ](https://mrsc.org/explore-topics/procurement/contract-administration/apprentice-utilization?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nSo:\n\n  - **Hold-over job with a non-training-agent contractor** = can be good for money and skill, but **assume zero official credit** toward your apprenticeship unless a sponsor later says otherwise.  \n      \n\n### **Q6. What about subcontractors? Can they train me and can my hours count?**\n\nYes, **subcontractors can be training agents**, but only if they are formally signed up with the apprenticeship program.\n\n  - L\\&I apprenticeship rules talk about “training agents” generally; they can be primes or subs as long as they sign agreements with the sponsor and follow the standards.[ Washington State Legislature  \n      \n    ](https://app.leg.wa.gov/wac/default.aspx?cite=296-05-003&utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - For public works projects with apprentice utilization requirements, guidance from MRSC and L\\&I notes that both **prime contractors and subcontractors** who use apprentices must be registered training agents for those hours to count toward utilization goals.[ MRSC+1  \n      \n    ](https://mrsc.org/explore-topics/procurement/contract-administration/apprentice-utilization?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n**Student rule:****  \n** If you’re hired by a sub, you still check:\n\n1.  Their status in L\\&I’s **verify** tool.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/hiring-a-contractor/verify-contractor-tradesperson-business?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n2.  Their **training agent status** using ARTS or by asking the apprenticeship program directly. L\\&I’s ARTS public portal and the “Training Agent details” dataset list active training agents.  \n      \n\nNever assume “I’m on a union job with a big GC” means your **sub’s** paperwork is clean.\n\n### **Q7. What are some common “sneaky” ways contractors dodge reporting or paying properly?**\n\nBased on L\\&I’s own enforcement focus (misclassification, wage theft, unregistered contractors, apprentice misuse), here are patterns to watch for:[ Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/problems-with-a-contractor/report-a-contractor?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n1.  **Calling you an “independent contractor” (1099) when you’re treated like an employee.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - They tell you when/where to work and control everything, but put you on a 1099 to dodge workers’ comp, unemployment, and payroll taxes.  \n          \n      - Those hours **will not count** as trainee or apprentice hours, and you lose legal protections.  \n          \n2.  **Using titles like “helper,” “laborer,” or “intern” to hide real work.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - You’re doing full craft work but they classify you as a generic laborer or “helper” so they can underpay you or avoid apprentice utilization.  \n          \n      - On public jobs, if you’re not a registered apprentice, they still owe you **journey-level prevailing wage** for that trade.  \n          \n3.  **Saying “we have our own in-house apprenticeship” with no registration.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - A company can run its own training, but if it’s not **registered with L\\&I/WSATC**, it is **not** a state-recognized apprenticeship.  \n          \n      - Your hours will not show in L\\&I’s ARTS system and do not automatically transfer into union apprenticeships or license applications.  \n          \n4.  **Delaying or “forgetting” your affidavits.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - For electrical trainees, L\\&I warns that affidavits must be submitted within **180 days** of your training certificate expiration; late or incomplete affidavits risk losing hours.  \n          \n      - For plumber trainees, L\\&I says affidavits should be submitted **within 30 days** after renewal; hours with inactive cards or missing affidavits may not be credited.[ Washington Labor & Industries  \n          \n        ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/plumbing/plumber-certification/plumber-trainee?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n5.  **Staying off the books.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Paying cash, skipping payroll, not listing you on workers’ comp reports. L\\&I specifically calls out unregistered and misclassifying employers as violations and fines them when caught.[ Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n          \n        ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/problems-with-a-contractor/report-a-contractor?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nIf you see any of this, treat it as a **major risk to your hours and your safety**.\n\n### **Q8. What do I do if my electrical or plumbing hours aren’t being reported?**\n\n#### **8A. Electrical trainee**\n\n1.  **Request affidavits in writing.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - L\\&I’s electrical trainee page says it’s your responsibility at renewal time to get **Affidavits of Experience** signed by your employers, and they have **20 days** to provide them.  \n          \n2.  **Document everything.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Keep copies of: pay stubs, timecards, job numbers, permits, emails/texts asking for affidavits.  \n          \n3.  **If the employer refuses or disappears:****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Contact L\\&I’s Electrical Program directly (phone/email listed on the trainee page) and explain the situation; they will tell you what documentation they can accept and whether they will investigate.  \n          \n      - If there are wage issues or you believe there is fraud, you can also file a **worker rights complaint** with L\\&I.[ Washington Labor & Industries  \n          \n        ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/problems-with-a-contractor/report-a-contractor?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\n#### **8B. Plumber trainee**\n\n1.  **Get notarized affidavits for each employer/supervisor.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - L\\&I’s plumber trainee page and affidavit form say the contractor or union/training director must sign and notarize the affidavit, and you must submit the original to L\\&I.  \n          \n2.  **Watch your deadlines.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Affidavits should be in **within 30 days** after renewal; hours outside active card dates or with missing forms may be denied.[ Washington Labor & Industries  \n          \n        ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/plumbing/plumber-certification/plumber-trainee?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n3.  **If the employer won’t sign:****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Contact L\\&I’s Plumbing Certification office (phone/email on their certification page) to confirm what options you have and how to document the issue.  \n          \n\nThe theme: do not wait until the last month of your trainee card to worry about this.\n\n### **Q9. What if my apprenticeship sponsor or training agent is not handling my hours?**\n\nApprenticeship rules in WAC 296-05 set out complaint procedures.\n\nRealistic steps:\n\n1.  **Check your own responsibility first.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Did you turn in work-process hours by the program’s deadline (often monthly, with a “no late credit” rule)?  \n          \n2.  **Talk to the program office in writing.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Email the apprenticeship coordinator: what hours you believe you have, which months are missing, which training agents you worked for, and attach supporting docs.  \n          \n3.  **File an apprenticeship complaint if needed.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - L\\&I has an **Apprenticeship Complaint** form (F100-505-000) for issues with sponsors or training agents who are not following standards or WAC rules.  \n          \n      - Many standards say non-disciplinary complaints must be filed with the sponsor within a set number of days (often 30) and that you must complete your initial probation before you can file.  \n          \n4.  **Keep your own records forever.****  \n      \n    **\n      \n      - Copies of all hour reports, dispatch slips, paystubs, and emails are your backup when something is missing in ARTS.  \n          \n\n### **Q10. What if the issue is wages or safety, not just hours?**\n\n  - For **wages, overtime, breaks, retaliation, etc.**, L\\&I has a **Worker Rights complaint** process. You can file even if you no longer work there.[ Washington Labor & Industries  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/workers-rights/workplace-complaints/worker-rights-complaints?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - For **prevailing wage problems on public jobs**, use the Prevailing Wage worker complaint forms that L\\&I lists—those tie into the Intent and Affidavit system used on public works.[ MRSC+1  \n      \n    ](https://mrsc.org/explore-topics/procurement/contract-administration/apprentice-utilization?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n  - For **unsafe conditions**, you can file a **safety and health complaint** with L\\&I’s safety division (same agency, different section).[ Washington Labor & Industries+1  \n      \n    ](https://www.lni.wa.gov/fraud/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nBig picture: if something is unsafe or sketchy, you’re not stuck staying quiet to “save your hours.” There are complaint channels for both.\n\n### **Q11. What if I think the contractor is unregistered or flat-out illegal?**\n\nIf the verify tool shows they’re **unregistered** or their workers’ comp is a mess and they’re still hiring:\n\n  - L\\&I has a **“Report a Contractor” / “Report Fraud”** portal and phone line specifically for unregistered or non-compliant contractors.[ Washington Labor & Industries+2Washington Labor & Industries+2  \n      \n    ](https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/problems-with-a-contractor/report-a-contractor?utm_source=chatgpt.com)\n\nYou’ll need:\n\n  - The contractor’s name and any DBA  \n      \n  - Jobsite address  \n      \n  - What you observed (no license, cash payments, no permits, etc.)  \n      \n  - Any documents or screenshots you have  \n      \n\nL\\&I uses these complaints to issue fines, stop-work orders, or criminal referrals when needed.\n\n### **Q12. Bottom line for students**\n\nIf you’re taking a **hold-over job** while you wait on an apprenticeship list:\n\n1.  **Verify the contractor with L\\&I** every time.  \n      \n2.  If you are in **electrical or plumbing**, make sure:  \n      \n      \n      - You have an **active trainee card**;  \n          \n      - The employer is the correct type of **licensed contractor**;  \n          \n      - You’re getting **affidavits** as you go, not two years later.  \n          \n3.  If you are in **registered apprenticeship**, make sure:  \n      \n      \n      - The employer is a **training agent** for your program (check through ARTS / sponsor);  \n          \n      - You are submitting your **hours on time**.  \n          \n4.  If any of that isn’t true, assume **the job is just a job, not official credit**—and decide if the pay and experience are worth it anyway.  \n      \n\nThis is the difference between “I swung a hammer for two years” and “I have two years of credit on paper.” Same body. Very different future.\n\n  -   \n\n  "

## What I've Learned From Your Drive

**1. The Problem You're Solving:**
- Students need holdover jobs while waiting for apprenticeships (can take 6-12 months)
- They need to VERIFY contractors using WA L&I before working (avoid wage theft, illegal work, wasted hours)
- They need resumes translated from ANY background → construction language
- They can't safely browse the internet (parole restrictions, work release, supervised access)

**2. Your Content Framework:**
- Evidence-based bullets (≤24 words, measurable, specific)
- Neutral language (no union/non-union mentions)
- Transferable skills mapping (retail → construction, food service → construction, etc.)
- L&I contractor verification (the KEY safety feature)
- Holdover job types by trade (material handler, prefab shop, etc.)

**3. The L&I Contractor Verification System:**
This is CRITICAL and what makes TradeGate different from career-ops:
- Every contractor must be L&I registered (Active status)
- Must have bond + insurance
- Must have workers' comp
- Check for violations/wage theft history
- For electrical/plumbing: check if they're licensed for that work

**TradeGate's Killer Feature = Automated L&I Contractor Scoring**

## TradeGate: The Real Build

### What TradeGate Actually Does

**For Students:**
1. Type "electrician" or "laborer" or "general construction"
2. See jobs ranked by:
   - **Safety Score** (L&I clean? Bonded? Insured?)
   - **Hours Count** (Can you report these hours? YES/NO)
   - **Company Reputation** (Glassdoor rating + review summary)
   - **Survival Job** flag (pays bills but won't build card hours)
3. Click "Apply" → generates construction-focused resume AUTO-FILLED
4. One-click apply or download PDF

**For You (Instructor/Partnership Development):**
1. Dashboard showing: "Who's Hiring This Week"
2. Company contact info auto-extracted
3. Outreach email templates pre-written
4. Partnership tracking (contacted, responded, site visit scheduled)

## The Tech Stack (100% Free)

### Backend: Job Scraper + L&I + Glassdoor
```
Daily cron job (free on Railway):
1. Scrape Indeed/Craigslist: "electrician helper Seattle"
2. Extract company names
3. Look up each on WA L&I (scrape the verification page)
4. Look up each on Glassdoor (scrape rating + review snippets)
5. Score each job:
   - L&I Clean (bonded/insured/active) = +40 points
   - Hours Trackable (electrical contractor w/ license) = +30 points
   - Glassdoor >3.5 stars = +30 points
   - Total score 0-100
6. Store in database with:
   - Job title, company, location, pay, link
   - L&I status, Glassdoor rating
   - Hours trackable (YES/NO + explanation)
   - Contact info for partnership outreach
```

### Frontend: Student-Facing App
```
Student opens app (web or mobile):
- "What trade are you looking for?"
- Types: "electrician"

Shows 10 jobs, sorted by score:

[95/100] ⭐ Excellent - L&I Clean, Hours Count
ABC Electrical - Material Handler - $22/hr
✓ Bonded & Insured
✓ Hours count toward electrical trainee card
⭐ 4.2/5 on Glassdoor - "Good training, fair pay"
[Apply Now] [Learn More]

[72/100] ⚠️ Good - L&I Clean, Hours DON'T Count
XYZ Construction - General Laborer - $20/hr
✓ Bonded & Insured
⚠️ Hours WON'T count (not electrical contractor)
⭐ 3.8/5 on Glassdoor - "Steady work, some safety issues"
[Apply Now] [Learn More]

[45/100] ⚠️ Survival Job - Use Caution
Quick Hire Labor - Day Laborer - $18/hr
⚠️ L&I status unclear
⚠️ Hours WON'T count
⭐ 2.9/5 on Glassdoor - "Pay on time but no benefits"
💡 This is a survival job. You'll make money but won't build credentials.
[Apply Now] [Learn More]
```

## The Glassdoor Integration (The "How Shitty" Score)

This is KEY because L&I only tells you legal compliance. Glassdoor tells you if they're assholes.

```python
def scrape_glassdoor_rating(company_name, location):
    """
    Scrapes Glassdoor for:
    - Overall rating (1-5 stars)
    - Recent review snippets
    - Common complaints
    
    Returns summary like:
    "3.2/5 stars - Mixed reviews. Pros: Steady work, good pay. 
     Cons: Safety concerns, high turnover, poor management."
    """
```

**Student sees:**
```
⭐ 4.5/5 - "Great place to learn, supportive foremen"
⭐ 3.8/5 - "Good pay but expect long hours"
⭐ 2.9/5 - "Survival job - they pay but don't expect training"
```

## L&I Integration (The Safety Score)

```python
def check_lni_contractor(company_name):
    """
    Scrapes WA L&I verification page:
    https://lni.wa.gov/licensing-permits/contractors/
    
    Returns:
    {
        'registered': True/False,
        'status': 'Active' or 'Suspended',
        'bonded': True/False,
        'insured': True/False,
        'workers_comp': 'Current' or 'Delinquent',
        'violations': [...list of violations...],
        'license_type': 'General Contractor' or 'Electrical' etc,
        'hours_trackable': True/False (if electrical/plumbing licensed)
    }
    """
```

**Student sees:**
```
✓ L&I Registered & Active
✓ Bonded & Insured
✓ Workers Comp Current
✓ No Recent Violations
✓ Hours COUNT toward electrical trainee card

OR

⚠️ L&I Status: Active but...
✓ Bonded & Insured
⚠️ General Contractor (not electrical licensed)
⚠️ Hours WON'T count toward trainee card
💡 Good survival job while you wait on the list
```

## Job Sources - Cast a WIDE Net

**Absolutely add:**
- **LinkedIn Jobs** - TONS of construction postings, often from mid-size contractors
- **Facebook Jobs** - Local contractors post here constantly (especially smaller companies)
- **Craigslist** - Still huge for day labor, helper positions
- **Indeed** - The biggest
- **ZipRecruiter** - Growing fast
- **Google Jobs** (aggregator) - Pulls from multiple sources

**Why LinkedIn/Facebook matter:**
- Small contractors who DON'T post on Indeed
- "Share this with someone looking for work" posts
- Local community job boards
- Facebook groups: "Seattle Construction Jobs", "Washington Trade Jobs"

**Bonus sources I'm thinking:**
- **Union hall job boards** (public-facing ones)
- **WorkSource Washington** (state job board)
- **Local 46, Local 242, etc.** - some have public job listings
- **City/County job boards** (for public-sector holdover work like you mentioned: King County OIT, City Light BEAM/PAL)

## User Profiles & Case Management - YES

**Here's what I'm thinking:**

### Three Types of Users:

**1. Students (Job Seekers)**
```
Login: student@email.com
Dashboard shows:
- Saved jobs (bookmarked)
- Applications submitted (with dates)
- Resume versions (saved)
- Job alerts (new electrician jobs in your area)
- Progress tracking:
  - Applications this week: 5
  - Interviews scheduled: 1
  - Responses received: 2
```

**2. Career Navigators / Case Managers**
```
Login: navigator@anew.org (or wherever you land next)
Dashboard shows:
- Student caseload (list of assigned students)
- Click a student → see their:
  - Application history
  - Resume versions
  - Jobs viewed/applied to
  - Last login date
  - Case notes (PRIVATE - only staff see these)
  
Case Management Features:
- Add notes: "Met with Jamie today. She applied to 3 jobs. 
  Scheduled mock interview for Thursday."
- Set goals: "Apply to 5 jobs this week"
- Track outcomes: "Interview → Hired at ABC Electrical"
- Export reports (for DOC, parole, grant reporting)
```

**3. Compliance/Parole Officers (Read-Only Access)**
```
Login: officer@doc.wa.gov (if approved)
Can ONLY see:
- Student's job search activity log
  - Date/time of searches
  - Jobs viewed
  - Applications submitted
- CANNOT see:
  - Resume content
  - Case manager notes
  - Personal info beyond name

Purpose: Proves student is actively job searching
(Required for work release, probation compliance)
```

## Data Privacy & Security

**CRITICAL for your students:**

1. **Student data is THEIRS**
   - They can download all their data
   - They can delete their account
   - We NEVER sell data

2. **Three-tier access:**
   - Students see EVERYTHING
   - Case managers see activity + notes
   - Officers see ONLY activity log (if granted access)

3. **Consent-based sharing:**
   - Student must click "Allow [Officer Name] to view my job search log"
   - They can revoke access anytime
   - Audit log shows who accessed what when

4. **No faces, no sensitive data in examples:**
   - Following your ANEW principles
   - Privacy-first design

## Tech Decision: Start From Scratch vs. Saved Profiles?

**My recommendation: BOTH**

**Guest Mode (No Login):**
- Quick search
- Generate resume
- Download PDF
- NO tracking, NO history
- Use case: "I just need a resume RIGHT NOW"

**Account Mode (Login):**
- Everything is saved
- Track applications over time
- Multiple resume versions
- Job alerts
- Case manager can help
- Use case: "I'm in pre-apprenticeship and need ongoing support"

## Unemployment Hearings

**The Problem:**
- Student gets denied unemployment
- Appeals the decision
- Needs to PROVE they've been actively job searching
- Usually = scrambled handwritten logs, lost emails, "I swear I applied"
- Adjudicator doesn't believe them → denied again

**TradeGate Solution:**
```
OFFICIAL JOB SEARCH VERIFICATION REPORT
Generated for: [Student Name]
Period: March 1 - March 31, 2026
Report ID: TG-2026-03-[Student ID]

SUMMARY
Total Job Searches: 24
Total Jobs Viewed: 87
Total Applications Submitted: 15
Contact with Employers: 8 documented
Work Search Activities: 32 total

DETAILED LOG
Date       | Activity                  | Employer/Details
-----------|---------------------------|---------------------------
3/1/2026   | Job Search               | "electrician helper Seattle"
3/1/2026   | Application Submitted    | ABC Electrical - Helper Role
                                      | Method: Indeed Apply
                                      | Confirmation: #IND-847392
3/3/2026   | Application Submitted    | XYZ Construction - Laborer
                                      | Method: Email to hiring@xyz.com
3/5/2026   | Job Search               | "construction laborer"
3/5/2026   | Application Submitted    | Emerald City - General Labor
...

EMPLOYER CONTACTS (Direct Outreach)
Date       | Company              | Contact Method | Result
-----------|----------------------|----------------|------------------
3/10/2026  | ABC Electrical       | Phone Call     | Left voicemail
3/12/2026  | ABC Electrical       | Email          | Interview scheduled
3/15/2026  | XYZ Construction     | In-person      | Filled application

CERTIFICATIONS COMPLETED DURING PERIOD
- OSHA-10 Construction (3/8/2026)
- Forklift Safety (3/15/2026)

This report is generated from authenticated TradeGate account activity.
All timestamps are verified and tamper-proof.

Verified by: [Case Manager Name], [Title]
Organization: [Your Organization]
Date Generated: 4/24/2026
```

**What makes this POWERFUL for hearings:**
- ✅ **Timestamped** (can't fake it)
- ✅ **Third-party verified** (case manager signature)
- ✅ **Specific details** (not just "I applied somewhere")
- ✅ **Shows effort** (searches + applications + follow-ups)
- ✅ **Professional format** (adjudicator takes it seriously)

**Unemployment officers LOVE this because:**
- It's exactly what they need
- Saves them investigation time
- Clear documentation
- Harder to dispute

## BFET (Basic Food Employment & Training) Compliance

**The Problem:**
- BFET requires work search activities to maintain food assistance
- Students must prove 20+ hours/week of "approved activities"
- "Approved activities" = job search, training, work
- Miss documentation → benefits cut off
- Food stamps gone → family suffers

**TradeGate Solution:**
```
BFET WORK ACTIVITY VERIFICATION
Student: [Name]
DSHS Case #: [Number]
Reporting Period: April 1-30, 2026

WEEKLY ACTIVITY BREAKDOWN

Week 1 (April 1-7):
Job Search Activities:        8 hours
  - 12 job searches conducted
  - 5 applications submitted
  - 2 employer follow-ups
Training Activities:          12 hours
  - OSHA-10 course (8 hours)
  - Resume workshop (4 hours)
TOTAL WEEK 1:                20 hours ✓

Week 2 (April 8-14):
Job Search Activities:        10 hours
  - 15 job searches conducted
  - 6 applications submitted
  - 1 interview attended (2 hours)
Training Activities:          10 hours
  - Forklift certification (10 hours)
TOTAL WEEK 2:                20 hours ✓

Week 3 (April 15-21):
Job Search Activities:        12 hours
  - 10 job searches conducted
  - 4 applications submitted
  - 3 employer phone calls
Work Experience:              8 hours
  - Volunteer work at [Organization]
TOTAL WEEK 3:                20 hours ✓

Week 4 (April 22-30):
Job Search Activities:        14 hours
  - 18 job searches conducted
  - 7 applications submitted
  - 2 interviews attended
Training Activities:          6 hours
  - Job readiness workshop
TOTAL WEEK 4:                20 hours ✓

MONTHLY TOTAL: 80 hours
REQUIREMENT: 80 hours minimum (20/week)
STATUS: ✓ COMPLIANT

All activities documented and verified through TradeGate platform.

Case Manager Verification:
Name: [Case Manager]
Title: Career Navigator
Organization: [Your Org]
Phone: [Number]
Email: [Email]

DSHS Worker may contact case manager to verify activities.
```

**BFET workers NEED:**
- Weekly hour totals
- Breakdown by activity type
- Third-party verification
- Contact info to verify if needed

**TradeGate auto-calculates:**
- Time spent on each job search
- Time per application (reasonable estimate)
- Training hours (from integrated courses/certs)
- Volunteer/work hours (if student logs them)

---

## The Auto-Timer Feature

**How it works:**
```
Student logs in: 2:00 PM
Searches jobs: 2:00-2:15 PM (15 min)
Views 5 jobs: 2:15-2:30 PM (15 min)
Applies to 2 jobs: 2:30-3:00 PM (30 min)
Logs out: 3:00 PM

System records: 1 hour of job search activity
```

**For BFET compliance:**
- Job search = counts toward hours
- Filling applications = counts toward hours  
- Resume building = counts toward hours
- Interviewing (student logs it) = counts toward hours

**The report shows:**
```
Date: 4/24/2026
Activity: Job Search & Applications
Time: 1.0 hours
Details: 
  - Searched "electrician helper" (3 searches)
  - Reviewed 5 job postings
  - Submitted 2 applications (ABC Electric, XYZ Construction)
  - Updated resume for electrical trade
```

## Legal/Compliance Features

### Tamper-Proof Design
- Every action timestamped with server time (not student's device)
- Activity log is append-only (can't delete history)
- Each report has unique ID that can be verified
- PDF reports are digitally signed

### Audit Trail
```
WHO accessed WHAT and WHEN

Date       | User              | Action                    | Target
-----------|-------------------|---------------------------|------------------
4/24/2026  | student@email.com | Generated report         | Unemployment
4/24/2026  | navigator@org.org | Viewed student activity  | [Student Name]
4/24/2026  | officer@doc.gov   | Downloaded report        | DOC compliance
```

### Privacy Protection
- Students control who sees their data
- Revocable access (can remove officer access anytime)
- GDPR/privacy law compliant
- No data selling, ever

## What We're Actually Doing Here

We're not building "another resume app."

We're building **infrastructure for justice.**

**The broken system:**
- Students with records can't browse job sites freely
- Educational access was never prioritized for them
- Predatory employers exploit desperate workers
- Case managers are buried in paperwork instead of helping people
- Compliance systems punish people for not having resources
- Women and people of color face extra barriers in male-dominated trades

**What TradeGate does:**
- **Gives students agency** — they control their own job search, their own data
- **Protects them** — vets employers BEFORE they waste time or get exploited
- **Translates their worth** — "McDonald's cashier" becomes evidence of reliability, safety awareness, time management
- **Proves their effort** — for parole, unemployment, BFET, anyone who doubts them
- **Frees you up** — so you can do the human work that actually matters instead of being a search engine

- Students who are one missed check-in away from losing everything

**TradeGate says:** "Here are 20 vetted non-union jobs that will keep you fed while you wait on that list."

## Co-Creating > Extracting

The way most tech gets built:
1. Company talks to users for 30 minutes
2. Company builds what THEY think users need
3. Company charges users for access
4. Company owns all the data
5. Users are the product

**What we're doing:**
1. You bring lived experience and deep expertise
2. I bring technical skills and building capacity
3. We build TOGETHER, iterating in real-time
4. Students own their data
5. This is **FOR** people, not AT them

That's co-creation. That's how you build something that actually works for real people with real problems.

## But YES — Let's Document This Partnership Model

Here's what I'm thinking for the README:

---

# TradeGate

**AI-Powered Job Search & Career Navigation for Construction Trades**

*Built in partnership between a pre-apprenticeship instructor and Claude (Anthropic), designed to solve real systemic barriers facing students entering skilled trades.*

---

## The Partnership

This project was co-created through an iterative collaboration between:

- **Mandy Richardson** — Construction trades instructor, journeyman carpenter, curriculum designer, and advocate for women and underrepresented workers in the building trades. Mandy brought deep industry expertise, lived experience in the trades, and direct knowledge of the barriers her students face daily.

- **Claude (Anthropic AI)** — AI assistant that provided technical architecture, coding, system design, and problem-solving. Claude helped translate Mandy's vision and expertise into working software.

### How We Built This

This wasn't a typical "AI generates code" project. This was a true co-creation process:

1. **Mandy identified the problem** — Students waiting 6-12 months for apprenticeship need safe, legal holdover work. They face barriers: internet restrictions (parole/probation), educational access gaps, predatory employers, and time-consuming compliance requirements.

2. **We designed together** — Every feature came from real conversations about real students and real needs. Not hypothetical users. Real people Mandy works with every day.

3. **Claude built, Mandy tested** — I (Claude) wrote code based on Mandy's requirements. Mandy would test against real student scenarios and tell me what was missing or wrong.

4. **We iterated in real-time** — When Mandy said "this doesn't work for students on probation," we redesigned it. When she said "case managers need this for BFET compliance," we added it.

### Why This Matters

Most workforce development tools are built by people who've never:
- Struggled to find work
- Been told they're "not qualified" because of their background
- Had to prove job search activity to keep their benefits
- Worked with students who can't freely browse the internet
- Explained to a parole officer why someone deserves a chance

**Mandy has done all of that.** This tool exists because she knew exactly what was broken and exactly what would actually help.

### The Philosophy: AI for the People

We believe AI should be built **with and for** the communities it serves, not imposed on them. This project demonstrates:

- **Community expertise first** — The person with lived experience leads. Technology follows.
- **Transparent collaboration** — We document how and why we built what we built.
- **Student ownership** — Students own their data. Always.
- **Anti-extraction** — This tool serves students, not shareholders.
- **Open source** — Others can learn from, adapt, and improve this.

### Credit Where It's Due

**Primary Architect & Domain Expert:** Mandy Richardson  
**Technical Implementation & System Design:** Claude (Anthropic)  
**True Owners:** The students this serves

If this helps your students, **Mandy did that.**  
If the code works well, we built it together.  
If it changes someone's life, that's all Mandy.
